Nikah — Marriage

Woman Cuts Man's Hand and Marries Him on That Act: Ruling on Mahr and Diya
Ruling with talil: a specific case of mahr and diya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr and diya when a woman injures a man and marries him on that injury, and explain why the specified mahr is invalid and why diya is paid from her own property.

Core Idea
If the specified mahr is a crime (like cutting a hand), it is invalid; she receives mahr al-mithl and must pay diya from her own property.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with an intersection of criminal injury (diya) and marriage (mahr). A woman intentionally cuts a man's hand, and then he marries her with the cutting as the dower. He subsequently dies from the injury. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the proper mahr for her status) and must pay the diya (blood money) from her own wealth, since the injury was intentional. The commentary explains why the cutting cannot be valid as mahr and why the 'aqila does not bear the diya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Read the first line: 'قطعت امرأة يد رجل عمداً أو تزوجها على اليد ثم مات'. What are the key facts? (Woman cuts man's hand intentionally, he marries her on that act, then he dies).
The word 'أو' could indicate two scenarios: either she cuts his hand, or he marries her on the cutting. The context suggests it's the same event.
2
Determine the legal obligations
Find the two obligations stated: 'فلها مهر مثلها والدية في مثلها'. She gets mahr al-mithl (her like's mahr) and must pay diya (blood money). Note that diya is on her property ('في مالها'), not on her 'aqila.
The phrase 'في مالها' indicates payment from her own wealth.
3
Understand why the specified mahr (the hand) is invalid
The specified mahr was the cutting of the hand, which is an act of qisas (retaliation). Qisas for a limb is not property and cannot be transferred as mahr. Therefore, the specification is invalid, and mahr al-mithl becomes due.
The commentator argues: 'التزوج على القصاص... وليس بمال'
4
Understand why diya is not on the 'aqila
For the 'aqila to pay diya, the injury must be mistaken (khat'a). Here the cutting was 'amd (intentional), so the 'aqila does not bear it. Diya is on the woman's own property.
The text states: 'والعاقلة لا تتحمل العمد'
5
Address the objection about qisas for killing
One might ask: Since the cutting was intentional and led to death, why is the woman not subject to qisas for death? The answer: The original obligation was qisas for the limb, but it fell due to inability (e.g., because of marriage or gender differences? Actually, the text says 'سقط للتعذر' then diya became due; when death occurred, it is considered an extension of the same injury, and since there was no pardon for the life, diya is due.
The commentator references al-Nihayah: 'لم لم يجب القصاص ههنا على المرأة'

Source Text

قطعت امرأة يد رجل عمداً أو تزوجها على اليد ثم مات فلها مهر مثلها والدية في مثلها وعلى عاقلتها لو خطأ يعني لو تزوج امرأة على قطعها يده عمداً فمات الزوج منه فلما مهر مثلها والدية في مالها وعلى عاقلتها لو خطأ وهذا قول الإمام. ولم يفصل المؤلف بين ما إذا مات قبل الدخول أو بعده لكن في قوله مهر المثل يشير إلى أنه بعد الدخول. وفي الكافي : إما أن يكون القطع عمداً أو خطأ وكل مسألة على ثلاثة أوجه: إما أن تزوجها على القطع أو على القطع وما يحدث منه أو على الجناية وقد برئ من ذلك أو مات، فإن كان القطع.. عمداً ذلك صحت التسمية وصار أرش اليد مهراً لها عندهم وبرئ من جميعاً. قال الشارح : فإذا كان القطع عمداً فهذا تزوج على القصاص في الطرف وهو ليس بمال على تقدير الاستيفاء وعلى تقدير وعلى تقدير السقوط أولاً، فإذا لم يصلح يصلح مهراً فيجب لها مهر المثل إذا مات ولا يجب القصاص لا يقال لا يجري القصاص بين الرجل والمرأة في الأطراف فكيف يكون تزويجاً عليه لأنا نقول : الموجب الأصلي في العمد القصاص وإنما سقط للتعذر ثم تجب عليه الدية فإذا سرى تبين أنه قتل ولم يتناوله العفو فتجب الدية لعدم العفو عن النفس وذلك في مالها لأن العاقلة لا تتحمل العمد. اهـ. قال في النهاية فإن قلت : لم لم يجب القصاص ههنا على المرأة على أن القطع كان عمداً وهي قتل من الابتداء
A woman cut off a man's hand intentionally, or he married her on the hand, then he died, so she gets her like's mahr and the diya on her property, and on her 'aqila if it was mistaken. Meaning, if a man married a woman on her cutting his hand intentionally, and the husband died from it, then she gets her like's mahr and the diya on her property, and on her 'aqila if it was mistaken. And this is the statement of the Imam. And the author did not distinguish between whether he died before consummation or after, but in his saying 'mahr al-mithl' it indicates that it is after consummation. And in al-Kafi: Either the cutting is intentional or mistaken, and each issue has three aspects: either she married him on the cutting, or on the cutting and what results from it, or on the injury, and he recovered from that or died. If the cutting was intentional, then the specification is valid and the compensation (arsh) of the hand becomes her mahr according to them, and he is free from all. The commentator said: So if the cutting is intentional, then this is marriage on retribution for the limb, and it is not property on the basis of executing it, and on the basis of dropping it firstly; so if it is not suitable as mahr, then her like's mahr is obligatory when he dies, and retribution is not obligatory. It cannot be said that retribution does not apply between man and woman in limbs, so how can marriage be upon it? For we say: The original obligation in intentional is retribution, but it falls due to inability, then diya becomes obligatory; so if it spreads (to death), it becomes clear that he was killed and the pardon did not cover it, so diya is obligatory due to lack of pardon for the life, and that is on her property because the 'aqila does not bear intentional. He said in al-Nihayah: If you say: why is retribution not obligatory here on the woman, since the cutting was intentional and she killed from the beginning?
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case: a woman intentionally cuts off a man's hand, or a man marries a woman on the basis of that cutting (i.e., the mahr is the hand that was cut). Then the man dies from the injury. The ruling, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, is that she gets mahr al-mithl (the proper mahr for her) and must pay the diya (blood money) from her own property because it was intentional; the 'aqila (tribe) only bears responsibility in cases of mistake. The author then comments that the ruling assumes the marriage was consummated (after entry). He then cites al-Kafi which outlines three scenarios regarding the marriage: marrying on the cutting only, on the cutting and its consequences, or on the injury (jinaya) in general, and whether the victim recovers or dies. If the cutting was intentional and he married on that act, the specification of the mahr as the cutting is valid, and the arsh (compensation) becomes the mahr, and the husband is free from all claims. The commentator explains that since the object of the marriage (the cutting) is qisas for the limb, which is not property, it cannot serve as mahr; therefore, proper mahr is due. The question of why qisas is not applied on the woman is answered: qisas was the original obligation, but it fell because of inability (presumably she is a woman and qisas in limbs may not apply? Actually, the text says 'qisas between man and woman in limbs does not apply'—this is a Hanafi principle that qisas for limbs is not applicable between man and woman due to difference in gender? Wait, the text says 'لا يقال لا يجري القصاص بين الرجل والمرأة في الأطراف' meaning 'it cannot be said that qisas does not apply between man and woman for limbs'. The commentator is refuting that objection: he says the original obligation is qisas, but it falls due to inability (maybe because she is a woman? Or because the husband died? Actually, the case is that she cut his hand, then he married her, then he died. So qisas for the hand could have been executed, but due to the marriage, it was dropped? The commentator explains that the primary obligation was qisas, but it fell because of inability (ta'azzur), then diya became due. When death occurred, it becomes clear that it was a killing, and since there was no pardon for the death, diya is due on her property. So the initial question about why qisas is not applied is answered by the fact that it fell due to impossibility.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr determined by her female relatives' mahr, due when the specific mahr is invalid.
العاقلة (al-ʿāqila): The tribal group responsible for paying diya in cases of accidental killing or injury.
أرش اليد (arsh al-yad): The compensation for cutting off a hand, which is a specific amount of diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a woman cuts a man's hand intentionally and then marries him on that act, what is the mahr she receives according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The cutting of the hand itself as mahr
B) The compensation (arsh) of the hand
C) Her like's mahr (mahr al-mithl)
D) No mahr because the cutting was a crime

Key Takeaway
When a mahr is specified as a crime (like cutting a hand), it is invalid, and the wife receives mahr al-mithl; additionally, if the crime causes death, the wife must pay diya from her own property if intentional, or through her 'aqila if mistaken.

Marriage on Intentional Injury Leading to Death
Ruling on marriage contracted on basis of intentional injury that leads to death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a woman marries a man on the basis of an intentional injury that leads to death, and explain why qisas is replaced by diyah and mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
Marrying on qisas for a limb is invalid as mahr, so mahr al-mithl and diyah are due.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq address a rare but instructive case: a woman cuts a man's hand intentionally, then marries him on that basis, and he later dies from the injury. The ruling clarifies the interplay of marriage, qisas, and diyah. Understanding this helps grasp the Hanafi principle that qisas is not property and cannot serve as mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a marriage contract conditioned on a woman cutting off a man's hand (intentional injury) that leads to his death. The ruling: the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper mahr) and must pay diyah (blood money) from her own wealth.
If the injury was accidental, diyah is on her 'aqilah.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogical reasoning): qisas for limb cannot be valid mahr because it is not property. Therefore, the marriage is treated as one without specified mahr, necessitating mahr al-mithl.
The original obligation in intentional injury is qisas, but it drops here due to impossibility.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: qisas is not property (mal) so it cannot constitute mahr. Hence the marriage contract is valid but without a specified mahr, similar to a marriage where mahr is not named at all.
The woman cannot pay qisas on herself, so diyah becomes due.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and response
An objection arises: qisas for limbs does not apply between man and woman, so how can marriage be based on it? The Hanafi response: qisas is the original right but falls due to impossibility; diyah substitutes.
This clarifies that the original right of qisas is not completely negated but replaced.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The ruling is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa (the Imam) and is relied upon in the Hanafi school. The author implies no dispute within the school on this specific case.
The commentary from al-Nihaya reinforces the reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قطعت امرأة يد رجل عمداً أو تزوجها على اليد ثم مات فلها مهر مثلها والدية في مثلها وعلى عاقلتها لو خطأ يعني لو تزوج امرأة على قطعها يده عمداً فمات الزوج منه فلما مهر مثلها والدية في مالها وعلى عاقلتها لو خطأ وهذا قول الإمام. ولم يفصل المؤلف بين ما إذا مات قبل الدخول أو بعده لكن في قوله مهر المثل يشير إلى أنه بعد الدخول. وفي الكافي : إما أن يكون القطع عمداً أو خطأ وكل مسألة على ثلاثة أوجه: إما أن تزوجها على القطع أو على القطع وما يحدث منه أو على الجناية وقد برئ من ذلك أو مات، فإن كان القطع عمداً ذلك صحت التسمية وصار أرش اليد مهراً لها عندهم وبرئ من جميعاً. قال الشارح : فإذا كان القطع عمداً فهذا تزوج على القصاص في الطرف وهو ليس بمال على تقدير الاستيفاء وعلى تقدير السقوط أولاً، فإذا لم يصلح مهراً فيجب لها مهر المثل إذا مات ولا يجب القصاص لا يقال لا يجري القصاص بين الرجل والمرأة في الأطراف فكيف يكون تزويجاً عليه لأنا نقول : الموجب الأصلي في العمد القصاص وإنما سقط للتعذر ثم تجب عليه الدية فإذا سرى تبين أنه قتل ولم يتناوله العفو فتجب الدية لعدم العفو عن النفس وذلك في مالها لأن العاقلة لا تتحمل العمد. اهـ. قال في النهاية فإن قلت : لم لم يجب القصاص ههنا على المرأة على أن القطع كان عمداً وهي قتل من الابتداء محال فإذا مات ظهر أن الموجب الأصلي هو القصاص ولما لم يصلح القصاص مهراً صار كأنه تزوج ولم يذكر شيئاً وفيه القصاص فكذا ههنا قلت نعم كذلك إلا أنه لما جعل القصاص مهراً جعل ولاية استيفاء القصاص للمرأة، ولو استوفت القصاص تستوفيه من نفسها وهو ولما سقط القصاص بقي النكاح بلا تسمية فيجب مهر المثل كما إذا لم يسم ابتداء ا هـ
If a woman cuts off a man's hand intentionally, or marries him on the basis of the hand, then he dies, she gets her mahr al-mithl and the diyah in her wealth, and on her 'aqilah if it was accidental. Meaning: If a woman marries a man on the basis of her cutting his hand intentionally and the husband dies from it, then for her is mahr al-mithl and the diyah in her wealth, and on her 'aqilah if it was accidental. This is the statement of the Imam. The author did not distinguish between death before or after consummation, but his saying 'mahr al-mithl' indicates it is after consummation. In al-Kafi: Either the cutting is intentional or accidental, and each case has three aspects: either she marries him on the cutting, or on the cutting and what occurs from it, or on the injury, and he recovers from that or dies. If the cutting was intentional, the naming (of mahr) is valid and the compensation for the hand becomes her mahr according to them, and he is absolved of all. The commentator said: So if the cutting was intentional, then this is marriage on qisas for a limb, which is not wealth on the basis of execution or on the basis of dropping. So if it is not suitable as mahr, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory for her when he dies, and qisas is not obligatory. It cannot be said that qisas does not apply between a man and a woman for limbs, so how can it be a basis for marriage? For we say: The original obligator in intentional injury is qisas, but it falls due to impossibility, then the diyah becomes obligatory. So when the injury spreads (causes death), it becomes clear that it was killing, and the forgiveness did not cover it, so the diyah becomes obligatory due to lack of forgiveness for the life, and that is in her wealth because the 'aqilah does not bear intentional injury. End. In al-Nihaya: If you say: Why is qisas not obligatory here upon the woman, given that the cutting was intentional and she killed from the beginning? It is impossible. So when he dies, it appears that the original obligator is qisas, and since qisas is not suitable as mahr, it is as if she married him without mentioning anything, and there is qisas in that, so similarly here. I say: Yes, indeed, except that when qisas was made the mahr, the right of executing qisas is given to the woman, and if she executes qisas, she executes it upon herself, and when qisas drops, the marriage remains without a named mahr, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory, just as if no mahr was named at the beginning. End.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanded by the commentator of al-Bahr al-Raiq. It addresses a specific case: a woman cuts off a man's hand intentionally, then marries him on the basis of that injury (i.e., the woman agrees to marry him in lieu of qisas for the cut), and then the man dies from the injury. The ruling is that the woman is entitled to Mahr al-Mithl (the proper mahr of a woman of her status) and must pay the diyah (blood money for the death) from her own wealth. If the cutting was accidental, the diyah is on her 'aqilah (her tribal guarantors). The commentator explains that the original obligation in intentional injury is qisas, but qisas for a limb cannot be made mahr because it is not property. Since qisas drops here (because the woman would have to execute it on herself, which is impossible), the marriage is treated as one without a named mahr, hence Mahr al-Mithl is due. The woman does not inherit from her husband because she is his killer. The commentary also addresses an objection: how can marriage be based on qisas if qisas for limbs is not applicable between men and women? The answer is that qisas is the original right, but due to impossibility (the woman cannot cut her own hand), it is replaced by diyah. The diyah becomes her obligation because the injury was intentional, so the 'aqilah does not bear it. The passage then discusses the point that when the man dies, it becomes clear that the original cause was qisas, but since it cannot be executed, the marriage contract is valid but without a specified mahr, leading to Mahr al-Mithl.

Key Terms
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliatory punishment equal to the injury caused, here specifically for limb cutting.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr of a woman of similar status to the bride, determined by her peers.
العاقلة (al-'aqilah): The group of paternal relatives (agnates) who pay diyah in cases of accidental homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman cuts a man's hand intentionally, then marries him on that basis, and he dies from the injury, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa?
A) She gets the diyah only.
B) She gets Mahr al-Mithl and pays the diyah in her own wealth.
C) She gets nothing because she killed him.
D) She gets the full compensation for the hand as mahr.

Key Takeaway
Marrying on qisas for a limb is invalid as mahr because it is not property, so the marriage remains valid with mahr al-mithl and diyah due to the woman for the death caused by intentional injury.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Marriage with Qisas as Mahr: Ruling and Legal Effect
Establishes the ruling that qisas cannot be mahr, so mahr al-mithl is due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when qisas is named as mahr and identify the consequence of an invalid mahr term.

Core Idea
If qisas is made the mahr, the mahr term is void but the marriage is valid, requiring mahr al-mithl.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Al-Bahr al-Raiq where a woman marries a man and names the qisas (retributive penalty) she is owed against him as her mahr. The passage clarifies the legal effect: qisas is not valid as mahr, so the marriage stands without a specified mahr, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. Understanding this distinction prevents the misconception that the marriage itself is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Marriage where qisas is named as mahr. State the overall hukm: the marriage is sahih (valid) but the mahr term is batil (void).
The validity of the marriage is independent of the mahr term in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Recognize the reason for invalidity of mahr
Why is qisas not valid as mahr? Because mahr must be property (mal) that can be owned and transferred; qisas is a personal retributive right, not property.
Qisas cannot be owned as property, so it cannot serve as mahr.
3
Apply qiyas to marriage without mahr
Since the mahr term is void, the situation is analogous to a marriage where no mahr is mentioned at the time of contract. In that case, mahr al-mithl is wajib.
The analogy (qiyas) is explicit: 'it becomes as if she married without mentioning anything'.
4
Determine the consequence
What is the required mahr? Mahr al-mithl (the appropriate mahr) becomes obligatory, just as in a marriage without a specified mahr. The woman is not entitled to qisas.
The man's death causes the qisas to fall, leaving only the obligation of mahr al-mithl.
5
Note cross-madhhab perspective
Though the Shafi'i school also requires mahr al-mithl in this scenario, they classify the mahr as fasid (defective) rather than void, but the practical outcome is the same.
The difference is primarily theoretical regarding the nature of the invalid mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا مات ظهر أن الموجب الأصلي هو القصاص ولما لم يصلح القصاص مهراً صار كأنه تزوج ولم يذكر شيئاً وفيه القصاص فكذا ههنا قلت نعم كذلك إلا أنه لما جعل القصاص مهراً جعل ولاية استيفاء القصاص للمرأة، ولو استوفت القصاص تستوفيه من نفسها وهو ولما سقط القصاص بقي النكاح بلا تسمية فيجب مهر المثل كما إذا لم يسم ابتداء ا هـ .
When he dies, it becomes clear that the original obligation is qisas. And since qisas is not valid as mahr, it becomes as if she married without mentioning anything, and in that case qisas applies. So here too. I said: Yes, likewise, except that when she made qisas the mahr, she made the right to execute qisas belong to her. If she executes qisas, she executes it upon herself. And when qisas falls, the marriage remains without a named mahr, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory, just as if no mahr was mentioned initially. End quote.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the legal effect of making qisas (retributive penalty) the mahr in a marriage contract. The commentator explains that if the woman marries a man on the condition that her claim of qisas against him is her mahr, and then the man dies from his injury, it becomes clear that the original obligation was qisas. Since qisas cannot serve as a valid mahr (because it is not property and cannot be owned), the naming of mahr is void. The marriage then stands without a specified mahr, and mahr al-mithl (appropriate mahr) becomes wajib, just as in a marriage where no mahr is mentioned at the outset. The commentator adds that in this case, the woman had the right to execute qisas herself, but since the man died, qisas falls, and only mahr al-mithl remains. This is an expansion of the base text's ruling, using qiyas (analogy) to the case of marriage without mahr.

Key Terms
القصاص (al-qisas): Retributive penalty for intentional bodily harm or murder, executed by the victim or their heirs.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The appropriate mahr determined by the mahr of women of similar status (family, beauty, wealth, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman marries a man and makes the qisas she is owed against him her mahr, and then he dies from his injury, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is batil (void) because mahr must be property.
B) The marriage is sahih and she is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
C) She is entitled to the full diya as mahr.
D) She receives nothing because qisas fell.

Key Takeaway
When qisas is invalid as mahr, the marriage is still valid and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.

Valid Mahr as Arsh: Recovery and Divorce Scenarios
Ruling statement with subcases on recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a marriage mahr is set as the arsh of a severed limb, and calculate the mahr due in the subcases of recovery with divorce after consummation, death, or divorce before consummation.

Core Idea
If the man recovers, the arsh becomes the mahr; full arsh after consummation/death, half arsh before.

This lesson examines the case where a marriage contract specifies the mahr as the value of a severed limb (arsh). The Hanafi school considers the marriage valid, but the amount due depends on whether the man recovers from the wound and whether the marriage is consummated or ended by divorce before consummation or death. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines these subcases with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a marriage contract where the mahr is set as the arsh (compensation) for a severed limb. According to the text, this marriage is valid (jā'iz).
2
Determine the mahr when the man recovers
If the man recovers from the wound, the naming of the mahr as arsh is effective. The arsh becomes her mahr.
3
Distinguish between post-consummation/death and pre-consummation divorce
If he divorces her after consummation or dies, she receives the full arsh. If he divorces her before consummation, she receives half the arsh because the effective mahr is considered five thousand (the arsh amount), and half is due before consummation.
The text mentions 'alfān wa khamsumi'a' (2500) as half, implying the arsh is 5000.
4
Consider the death scenario from the wound
If the man dies from the wound, the naming of the mahr becomes void by consensus. She is not entitled to the arsh; instead, she receives mahr al-mithl (after consummation) or mut'ah (before consummation).
This will be detailed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تزوجها على موجب القطع جاز فإن طلقها بعد الدخول بها أو مات عليها سلم لها جميع الأرش، وإن طلقها قبل الدخول بها سلم لها من ذلك ألفان وخمسمائة ورد على الزوج ألفان وخمسمائة لأنه تزوجها في الحاصل على خمسة آلاف فإن طلقها قبل الدخول بها يسلم لها نصف ذلك ويلزمها أن ترد النصف على الزوج. هذا إذا أبرئ من القطع، وإن مات من ذلك فالتسمية باطلة عندهم جميعاً ولها مهر مثلها وقيد بقوله «مهر مثلها» المفيد أنه بعد الدخول لا قبل الدخول فلها المتعة ثم القياس أن لا تجب عليها الدية في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي الاستحسان تجب الدية في مالها وعلى قولهما صح العفو ولم يكن عليها لا قصاص ولا دية لو مات هذا إذا تزوجها على القطع قيد بذكر اليد فقط لأنه إذا تزوجها على القطع وما يحدث منه إن برئ من ذلك صار أرش يده مهراً لها عندهم جميعاً ويسلم لها ذلك، وإن كان أكثر من مهرها مثلها، وإن مات من ذلك بطلت التسمية وكان لها مهر مثلها وسقط القصاص مجاناً بغير شيء ولا ميراث لها من زوجها لأنها قاتلته وعليها عدة المتوفى عنها زوجها.
If she marries him on the value of the cut (wound), it is permissible. If he divorces her after consummation or dies, she receives all the arsh (compensation). If he divorces her before consummation, she receives two thousand five hundred from that, and she returns two thousand five hundred to the husband, because he married her in effect on five thousand. If he divorces her before consummation, she receives half of that, and she must return half to the husband. This is if he recovers from the cut. If he dies from it, the naming is void according to all of them, and she is entitled to mahr al-mithl. And he restricted by his saying 'mahr al-mithl' indicating that after consummation, not before; so she gets pleasure-gift. Then by qiyas, the diya is not wajib upon her according to Abu Hanifa; but by istihsan, the diya is wajib upon her wealth. According to the two Sahibayn, the forgiveness is valid, and neither qisas nor diya is upon her. This is if she marries him on the cut, restricted by mention of the hand only. Because if she marries him on the cut and what results from it, if he recovers, his hand's arsh becomes her mahr according to all, and it is given to her, even if it is more than her mahr al-mithl. If he dies from it, the naming is void, and she is entitled to mahr al-mithl, and qisas falls for free without anything, and she does not inherit from her husband because she killed him, and she must observe the waiting period of a widow.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of rulings on marriage when the mahr is the value of a limb (qat'). It covers multiple subcases. First, if the man recovers, the arsh (compensation for the limb) becomes the mahr. If he divorces her after consummation or dies, she receives the full arsh. If he divorces her before consummation, she receives half, because the mahr was effectively five thousand (the arsh amount). If the man dies from the wound, the naming of mahr is void by consensus, and she receives mahr al-mithl. The commentator notes that mahr al-mithl applies after consummation; before consummation, she gets mut'ah (pleasure-gift). Then there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: by qiyas, Abu Hanifa says diya is not wajib upon her; by istihsan (preferred), diya is wajib from her wealth. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the forgiveness (through marriage) is valid, and no qisas or diya is upon her. The passage also clarifies that if she marries on the cut and what results from it, the arsh becomes mahr if he recovers; if he dies, naming is void. She does not inherit because she is the killer, and she must observe 'iddah of widow.

Key Terms
الأرش (al-arsh): Compensation for loss of a limb or organ, specific amount fixed by shariah.
قيد بذكر اليد (qayyada bi-dhikr al-yad): The commentator restricts the ruling to cases where only the hand is mentioned in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman marries a man with mahr set as arsh of his right hand (5000 dirhams). He recovers from the wound and divorces her before consummation. How much mahr is due?
A) 5000 dirhams (full arsh)
B) 2500 dirhams (half arsh)
C) 0 dirhams (mahr al-mithl)
D) 5000 dirhams plus mut'ah

Key Takeaway
When mahr is set as arsh and the man recovers, the mahr is valid: full arsh after consummation or death, half arsh before consummation.

Death from the Wound: Void Mahr, Mahr al-Mithl, and Consequences
Ruling statement on death from the wound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that if the husband dies from the wound, the mahr naming is void, and apply the rules of mahr al-mithl, no inheritance, and iddah of a widow.

Core Idea
If he dies from the wound, the mahr naming is void; she gets mahr al-mithl, no inheritance, and must observe iddah.

When the husband dies as a direct result of the wound that was the subject of the mahr, the Hanafi school rules that the mahr specification becomes void by consensus. This lesson covers the consequences: mahr al-mithl (or mut'ah if before consummation), the dropping of qisas, the prohibition of inheritance due to the wife causing the death, and the requirement of widow's iddah. The passage also restricts the ruling to the hand specifically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the death scenario
The scenario is when the husband dies from the wound (the 'cut') that was the basis of the mahr. This is distinct from death from other causes after recovery.
2
State the ruling on the mahr naming
According to the text, the naming of the mahr as arsh is void (bāṭila) by agreement of all Hanafi authorities. The mahr is not the arsh.
Void means it is as if no mahr was specified.
3
Determine the mahr due
If the marriage was consummated, she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (fair mahr for a woman of her status). If not consummated, she receives mut'ah (pleasure-gift), not half the arsh.
The commentator clarifies 'qayyada bi-qawlihi mahr al-mithl al-mufīd annahu ba‘da al-dukhūl lā qablahu' – meaning that mahr al-mithl is only after consummation.
4
Apply the ancillary rules
The wife does not inherit from her husband because she is the cause of his death (qātila). She must observe the waiting period of a woman whose husband has died (ʿiddat al-mutawaffā ʿanhā zawi̊hā).
The text states 'lā mirātha lahā min zawjihā li-annahā qātalathu'.

المتعة (al-mut'ah): A pleasure-gift given to a divorced woman before consummation when no mahr has been specified.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Diya Liability When Wife Causes Husband's Death
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diya liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa qiyas, istihsan, and Sahibayn) regarding diya liability when the wife's injury causes the husband's death, and evaluate which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's qiyas: no diya; istihsan: diya wajib; Sahibayn: forgiveness valid, no diya.

This lesson delves into the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the wife must pay diya (blood money) if her husband dies from the wound that was the basis of the mahr. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three views: Abu Hanifa's qiyas (no diya), the istihsan position (diya wajib on her wealth), and the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that forgiveness through marriage is valid, absolving her of qisas and diya. Understanding this dispute requires knowing the usul principles of qiyas vs. istihsan and the concept of 'afw (forgiveness).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether the wife owes diya when the husband dies from the wound that was the subject of the mahr. The context: she caused the wound, albeit in a situation that may imply forgiveness due to the marriage contract.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position by qiyas
Al-qiyās: According to Abu Hanifa, by strict analogy, the wife is not liable for diya because the wound was inflicted in a context where qisas is not applicable (due to the marriage). The passage says 'al-qiyās an lā tajiba ʿalayhā al-diya fī qawl Abī Ḥanīfa'.
Qiyas here means analogy to cases where injury is forgiven.
3
State the istihsan position
By istihsan (juristic preference), she is required to pay diya from her own wealth. This is the position preferred by later Hanafi scholars (mufta bihi). The passage says 'wa fī al-istiḥsān tajibu al-diya fī mālihā'.
Istihsan overrides qiyas due to a stronger consideration, likely the preservation of the victim's rights.
4
State the position of the Sahibayn
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the marriage contract itself implies forgiveness (ʿafw). Therefore, she is not liable for either qisas or diya. The passage says 'wa ʿalā qawlihimā ṣaḥḥa al-ʿafwu wa lam yakun ʿalayhā lā qiṣāṣ wa lā diya'.
The Sahibayn consider the marriage as a form of amicable settlement.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and tarjih
The later Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Marghinani, Ibn Nujaym) adopt the istihsan position, making diya wajib on her wealth. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah for the istihsan view.

Source Text

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying the ruling of an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from qiyas in favor of a stronger consideration.
العفو (al-ʿafw): Forgiveness; waiving of a right (e.g., qisas or diya).

A) No liability (by qiyas)

C) Forgiveness valid, no diya (Sahibayn)
D) Diya wajib but on the husband's estate

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three positions on diya in this case; the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) is that diya is wajib on the wife's wealth by istihsan.

Marriage of a Woman Who Killed by Mistake to the Wali on the Diya
Ruling on marriage to the wali of the deceased on the diya due on the 'aqila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a marriage where the mahr is the diya due on the 'aqila and explain the discharge of the 'aqila's liability.

Core Idea
Marrying the wali on the diya is valid; the 'aqila are discharged.

This lesson examines a unique intersection of nikah and diyat: a woman accidentally kills a man, and then marries his wali (guardian) agreeing that the diya owed by her 'aqila becomes her mahr. The Hanafi school rules this marriage valid and the 'aqila fully discharged. We will unpack the reasoning, the consequences, and contrast with views of other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
A woman kills a man by mistake (khata). The diya is wajib on her 'aqila. She then marries the wali of the deceased, with the diya as the mahr. The question: is this marriage valid?
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The text says 'that is valid' (ja'iz). The marriage is sahih. The 'aqila are discharged from the diya because the diya becomes the mahr.
The diya is a debt, but it can be transferred as mahr with the consent of the parties.
3
Analyse the consequence of divorce before consummation
If the husband divorces her before consummation, he can claim half the diya from the 'aqila, because half the mahr is prescribed in that case.
This shows that the 'aqila remain liable for half the diya if the marriage ends before consummation.
4
Contrast with other schools (al-mukhtalaf fih)
Imam Malik holds the marriage invalid because diya is a debt, not property that can be given as mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i allows it if the diya is a known amount.
Hanafi position is that a known debt can be mahr, as long as it is specified.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
In a modern context, if a woman's insurance company is liable for accidental death compensation, she could marry the victim's heir agreeing to transfer the compensation as mahr. Hanafi ruling would allow it.
The illa (effective cause) is that the liability is a known financial obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا إذا تزوجها المقطوع يده، فلو تزوجها وليه قال امرأة قتلت رجلاً خطأ فتزوجت ولي المقتول على الدية التي وجبت على العاقلة فذلك جائز والعاقلة برأت فإن طلقها قبل الدخول بها رجع على العاقلة بنصف الدية رجل شج رجلاً موضحة عمداً أو صالحه المشجوج عن الموضحة وما يحدث منها على مال مسمى قبضه ثم شجه رجل آخر موضحة عمداً ومات من الموضحتين فعلى الآخر القصاص ولا شيء على الأول، وكذلك لو كان الصلح مع الأول بعد ما شجه الآخر قال أبو الفضل : فقد استحسن في موضع آخر من هذا الكتاب أن له القصاص على الآخر إذا كان شجه بعد صلح الأول رجل شج رجلاً موضحة عمداً وصالحه عنها وما يحدث عنها على عشرة آلاف درهم وقبضها ثم شجه آخر خطأ ومات منها فعلى الثاني خمسة آلاف درهم على عاقلته ويرجع الأول في ماله المقتول بخمسة آلاف درهم، وإن كانت الشجتان عمداً جاز إعطاء الأول وقتل الآخر؛ الأسبيجابي جامع الفتاوى ..
This is if the man with the cut hand marries her. If her guardian marries her: he said, a woman killed a man by mistake, then she married the wali of the killed man on the diya that was wajib upon the 'aqila. That is valid, and the 'aqila are discharged. If he divorces her before consummation, he has recourse to the 'aqila for half the diya. A man wounded another intentionally causing a head wound (mudiha), or the wounded settled with him for the mudiha and what results from it for a named amount, which he received. Then another man wounded him intentionally with a mudiha, and he died from the two mudihas. The latter is subject to qisas, and nothing is upon the former. Likewise, if the settlement with the first was after the second wounded him. Abu al-Fadl said: He has approved in another place of this book that he has qisas against the second if he wounded him after the settlement with the first. A man wounded another intentionally with a mudiha and settled with him for it and what results from it for ten thousand dirhams, and he received it. Then another wounded him by mistake and he died from it. The second owes five thousand dirhams upon his 'aqila, and the first recovers from the wealth of the killed man five thousand dirhams. If both wounds are intentional, it is permissible to give the first and kill the second; al-Isbijabi, Jami' al-Fatawa.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage introduces a new scenario: a woman kills a man by mistake, and then marries the wali (guardian) of the deceased on the diya that was wajib upon her 'aqila (tribal guarantors). The commentator rules that this marriage is valid, and the 'aqila are discharged from liability. If the husband divorces her before consummation, he can claim half the diya from the 'aqila. Then the passage moves to a different case: two men wound a victim, one by settlement, the other later. Key rulings: if the settlement is with the first, and the second intentionally wounds causing death, the second faces qisas, and the first is free. Abu al-Fadl notes a stronger opinion (istihsan) that qisas applies to the second if he wounded after the settlement. Then a case of one intentional settlement and one accidental wound: the second's 'aqila pay half diya, and the first recovers from the deceased's estate. If both wounds were intentional, the first can be given (compensation) and the second killed. This shows the complexity of multiple injuries and settlements.

Key Terms
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The male relatives on the father's side who are responsible for paying diya in cases of accidental killing.
الصلح (al-sulh): A settlement between the victim or his heirs and the offender to waive qisas for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman accidentally kills a man and then marries his wali on the diya that was wajib upon her 'aqila, what happens to the 'aqila's liability?
A) They remain liable for half the diya.
B) They are fully discharged from the diya.
C) The woman must pay the diya from her own wealth.
D) The marriage is invalid, so the diya remains.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law validates a marriage where the mahr is a known diya, discharging the 'aqila from their liability.

Effect of Marriage on 'Aqila Liability for Mahr
States ruling on 'aqila liability when marrying a criminal woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how marriage to a female criminal affects the 'aqila's diya liability and calculate the balance payable when mahr al-mithl is less than diya.

Core Idea
Marriage reduces 'aqila liability by mahr al-mithl; they pay the leftover to the husband's heirs.

This lesson examines a specific intersection of nikah and diyat. When a man marries a woman who has committed a crime (such as qisas leading to amputation), the marriage contract creates a new financial obligation (mahr) that interacts with the 'aqila's existing liability. The Hanafi school rules that the 'aqila's burden is reduced by the amount of mahr al-mithl, ensuring the victim's heirs still receive compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A man marries a woman who has committed a crime (jinaaya) that imposes a diya obligation on her 'aqila (paternal relatives). The marriage is valid, and the dower is mahr al-mithl (proper dower) since no specific amount is mentioned.
2
State the default 'aqila liability
In cases of accidental killing or injury, the 'aqila is obliged to pay diya to the victim's heirs. The default amount for a life is 5,000 dirhams (for a man) – though amounts vary by school and era.
Hanafi: 5,000 dirhams for accidental killing.
3
Apply the marriage effect
The marriage contract makes mahr al-mithl payable to the wife. This amount becomes her property and offsets the 'aqila's liability. The 'aqila is relieved of paying up to the amount of mahr al-mithl.
The reduction applies even if the marriage is contracted on the basis of the crime itself.
4
Determine the balance
If mahr al-mithl is less than the full diya, the 'aqila must pay the difference to the husband's heirs (the victim's heirs). If mahr equals or exceeds diya, the 'aqila pays nothing.
The passage gives the example: if mahr al-mithl cannot cover diya entirely, the balance is paid to the husband's heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكذا يسقط عن العاقلة خمسة ألاف وإن كان لا يخرج فبقدر ما يخرج من الثلث مقدار مهر مثلها يسقط عن العاقلة ويردون الباقي إلى ورثة الزوج وكذلك إن تزوجها على الجناية فالجواب فيه من أوله إلى آخره كالجواب فيما إذا تزوجها على القطع
Thus, five thousand are deducted from the 'aqila. If it does not come out [entirely], then to the extent that comes out from one-third, the amount of her mahr al-mithl is deducted from the 'aqila, and they return the remainder to the husband's heirs. Similarly, if he married her on account of the crime, the entire answer from beginning to end is like the answer in the case where he married her on account of the amputation.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It explains the effect on the 'aqila when a man marries a woman who has committed a crime (jinaaya) such as having her hand amputated in qisas. The mahr (dower) in such a marriage is mahr al-mithl (the proper dower). The 'aqila (the group responsible for paying diya) is relieved of liability up to the amount of mahr al-mithl. If mahr al-mithl is less than the full diya (5,000 dirhams), the 'aqila pays only the difference to the husband's heirs. The same ruling applies whether the marriage is contracted on the basis of the amputation (cut) or on the basis of the crime itself. This is a concise statement of the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
العاقلة (al-'āqila): The group of paternal relatives (asaba) responsible for paying diya in cases of accidental killing or injury.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower appropriate for a woman of her status, used when no dower is specified or when the specified dower is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Marriage to a female criminal reduces the 'aqila's diya liability by the amount of mahr al-mithl; the 'aqila pays the remainder to the husband's heirs.

Validity of Marriage with Diya as Dower
Ruling on marriage with diya as dower and its effect on 'āqila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding a marriage contracted with diya as dower and explain the effect on the 'aqila's obligation.

Core Idea
Marriage with diya as dower is valid; the 'aqila is discharged, but half can be reclaimed on pre-consummation divorce.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a woman who accidentally killed a man marries the victim's heir on the condition that the diya becomes her dower. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the validity of such a marriage and its financial consequences. Understanding this ruling requires appreciating how the Hanafi school treats diya as a valid consideration in a marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Parties and Scenario
A woman commits accidental killing (khatāʾ) of a man. She then marries the victim's heir (walī al-maqtūl) on the condition that the diya (blood money) owed by her 'āqila becomes the dower (mahr).
The 'āqila is the group responsible for paying diya, typically the woman's tribe or insurer.
2
Determine the Ruling (Hukm) of the Marriage
The passage rules the marriage jāʾiz (permissible/valid). The diya, being a fixed financial right, is valid consideration for marriage.
The ruling is based on the principle that any legitimate property can serve as dower.
3
Identify the Proof: Analogy (Qiyas)
The proof is qiyas: marriage with a known debt (diya) is analogous to marriage with any valid dower. Since diya is a fixed and payable financial obligation, it qualifies as a valid mahr.
The underlying ʿilla (effective cause) is both involve a financial right that is considered property (mal mutaqawwim).
4
Work Through the Consequences
As a result of the valid marriage, the 'āqila is discharged from their diya obligation. If the husband divorces before consummation, he recovers half the diya from the 'āqila (as half the dower is due). After consummation, the full dower is fixed, and no recovery occurs on divorce.
This mirrors standard rules of mahr: before consummation, wife gets half; after, full.
5
Note the Underlying Principle
The Hanafi school treats a known debt as valid subject matter for a contract. This extends to marriage, where the dower need not be in hand at the time of contract, as long as it is determinable and legally owned.
This differs from schools requiring immediate delivery or full certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا إذا تزوجها المقطوع يده، فلو تزوجها وليه قال امرأة قتلت رجلاً خطأ فتزوجت ولي المقتول على الدية التي وجبت على العاقلة فذلك جائز والعاقلة برأت فإن طلقها قبل الدخول بها رجع على العاقلة بنصف الدية
This applies if he married the woman whose hand was cut off. But if her guardian married her: He said: A woman killed a man accidentally, so she married the guardian of the deceased on the condition of the diya that was due upon the 'aqila – that is permissible, and the 'aqila is discharged. If he divorces her before consummation, he recovers half the diya from the 'aqila.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of marriage in relation to jinaaya. It first notes that the previous rule (about mahr al-mithl) applies when the woman herself marries. But if her guardian (wali) marries her, a different case is considered: a woman accidentally kills a man, and then she marries the victim's heir (the guardian who has the right to diya) on the condition that the marriage dower is the diya due from her 'aqila. This marriage is valid. As a result, the 'aqila is freed from the diya obligation because they have now become the dower. However, if the husband divorces her before consummation, he can recover half the diya from the 'aqila (since half the dower is due in case of divorce before consummation). The ruling is based on analogy: just as a marriage with an invalid dower results in mahr al-mithl, here the dower is the diya itself, which is valid consideration, so the marriage is valid.

Key Terms
ولي المقتول (walī al-maqtūl): The heir or guardian of the deceased who has the right to claim qisas or diya.
الدية (ad-diya): Blood money paid to the victim's heirs in cases of accidental killing or where qisas is waived.
العاقلة (al-ʿāqila): The group (tribe or insurer) responsible for paying diya on behalf of the killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The marriage is valid and the 'āqila is freed from the diya.
C) The 'āqila remains liable and the dower is separate.
D) The marriage requires a separate dower.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates marriage with diya as dower, freeing the 'āqila, with a possible half-recovery upon pre-consummation divorce.

Marriage with Invalid Dower: Mahr al-Mithl and the Effect of Jinaaya on 'Aqila
Matn and commentary on marriage with jinaaya as dower, covering both intentional and accidental cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when a marriage is contracted with a crime as dower, state that the wife receives mahr al-mithl, and analyze the effect of accidental death on the 'aqila and the husband's bequest.

Core Idea
Marriage on condition of jinaaya is valid, but the specified dower is void; in accidental death, the 'aqila is relieved and the husband's bequest of diya is subject to the one-third rule.

In this lesson, we examine a unique scenario from the Hanafi school: a man marries a woman on the condition that her hand (as qisas) or the crime itself becomes the dower. The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary in al-Bahr al-Raiq provide the ruling. We will see that the marriage is valid but the dower is void, so the wife receives her proper dower (mahr al-mithl). Then, in the case of accidental injury, the 'aqila is relieved of the diya, and the husband's estate handles the matter as a bequest. This passage illustrates the interplay of marriage, diyat, and wasiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and core ruling
The matn states: if a man marries a woman on account of the hand (as qisas) or the crime, and she dies from it, she gets mahr al-mithl. Note that the marriage itself is valid.
2
Understand why the specified dower is void
The commentary explains by analogy to marriage with wine or pig: the hand or crime is not valid property, so the dower specification is void. The marriage remains valid, so mahr al-mithl is due.
Qiyas to wine/pig: asl = marriage with non-property dower, hukm = dower void, ʻilla = dower is ghayr mutaqawwim.
3
Examine the accidental case
If the injury is accidental, the diya is on the 'aqila, but since the marriage contract made the diya the dower, it becomes the wife's property, relieving the 'aqila. The husband's estate effectively bequeaths the diya to the 'aqila, subject to the one-third rule.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a dispute whether the portion of the killer (husband if he caused the injury) drops. The more correct view (asahh) is that the entire bequest is effective, based on a logical argument to avoid infinite regression.
The commentator sides with the asahh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن تزوجها على اليد وما يحدث منها أو على الجناية فمات منه فلها مهر المثل كما لو تزوجها على خمر أو خنزير وقد تقدم قال رحمه الله : (ولا شيء عليها) لأنه رضي بسقوط القصاص على أنه يصير مهراً وهو لا يصير مهراً فسقط أصلاً فصار كما إذا سقط القصار بشرط أن لا يصير مالاً فإنه يسقط مجاناً وقد تقدم. قال رحمه الله : (ولو خطأ العاقلة رفع عن مهر مثلها ولهم ثلث ما ترك وصية لأن التزوج على اليد وما يحدث منها أو على الجناية تزوج على موجبها وموجبها هنا الدية وهي تصلح مهراً فصحت التسمية إلا أنه يقدر مهر مثلها يعتبر من جميع المال لأنه ليس فيه محاباة والمريض لا يجر عليه من التزوج لأنه من الحوائج الأصلية فينفذ قدر مهر مثلها من جميع المال، وما زاد على ذلك الثلث لأنه من تبرع والدية على عاقلتها وقد صارت مهراً فيسقط كلها عنهم إن كان مهر مثلها مثل الدية أو أكثر، ولا يرجع عليهم بشيء لأنهم كانوا يتحملون عنها بسبب جنايتها، فإذا صار ذلك ملكاً لها يسقط عنهم أصلاً فلا يغرمون لها، وإن كان مهر مثلها أقل من الدية سقط أيضاً لأنه وصيته لهم فيصح لأنهم أجانب، وإن كان لا يخرج من الثلث سقط وأدوا الزيادة إلى الولي لأن الوصية لا نفاذ لها إلا من الثلث ثم قيل لا يسقط قدر نصيب القاتل لأن الوصية للقاتل لا تصح والأصح أنه يسقط كله لأنه أوصى لمن تجوز له الوصية فهو كمن أوصى لحي وميت فإن الوصية كلها تكون للحي، ولأنه لو لم يسقط نصيبه لكان ذلك القدر هو الواجب بالقتل فتتحمله العاقلة عنه فينقسم أيضاً فيلزم مثل ذلك عن نصيبه أيضاً ثم هكذا وهكذا إلى أن لا يبقى منه شيء، فلو أبطلنا الوصية في صحته ابتداء لزمنا أن لا يسقط شيء
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if he marries her on account of the hand and what arises from it, or on account of the crime, and she dies from it, she gets mahr al-mithl, just as if he married her for wine or a pig, and it has preceded. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And nothing is owed by her) because he consented to the dropping of qisas on the condition that it becomes a dower, but it does not become a dower, so it falls entirely, as if qisas fell on condition that it does not become property, so it falls for free, and it has preceded. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if it was accidental, the 'aqila is relieved of her mahr al-mithl, and they get one-third of what he left as a bequest (wasiyya), because marriage on account of the hand and what arises from it or on account of the crime is marriage on its consequence, and its consequence here is the diya, which is suitable as a dower, so the specification is valid. However, her mahr al-mithl is calculated from all the property because there is no favoritism, and the sick person is not harmed by marriage because it is one of the basic needs, so the amount of her mahr al-mithl is executed from all the property, and what is over and above that is from one-third because it is a donation. The diya is upon her 'aqila, and it has become dower, so it is all dropped from them if her mahr al-mithl is equal to the diya or more, and they are not required to pay anything because they were bearing it on account of her crime. When that became her property, it falls from them entirely, so they do not pay it to her. If her mahr al-mithl is less than the diya, it also falls because it is his bequest to them, and it is valid because they are outsiders. If it does not come out of one-third, it falls and they pay the excess to the guardian because a bequest is only effective from one-third. Then it was said: The portion of the murderer does not drop because a bequest to the murderer is not valid. The more correct view is that it all drops, because he made a bequest to those for whom bequest is permissible, so it is like one who bequeaths to a living person and a dead person; the entire bequest goes to the living. And because if his portion did not drop, that amount would be what is obligatory for the killing, but the 'aqila bears it for him, so it would also divide, and the same would be repeated from his portion, and so on until nothing remains. Thus, if we invalidate the bequest in its validity from the beginning, it would require that nothing drops.)
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This is the matn (from Kanz al-Daqaiq) and its commentary from the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq. The matn states the core ruling: if a man marries a woman on the condition of her hand being cut (as a result of qisas) or on the condition of the crime itself, and she later dies from that injury, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper dower), not the specified dower (the hand or the crime), because that specified dower is invalid (like wine or pig). This is because the agreement to drop qisas in exchange for marriage is effectively a conditional waiver, but since the condition is that the property (hand) becomes dower, and it cannot, the dower is void and she gets mahr al-mithl. The commentary then explains that, in the case of accidental injury (where the 'aqila is liable), the 'aqila is relieved of the mahr al-mithl amount because it becomes the wife's property, and the husband's heirs get one-third of his estate as a bequest (since the husband effectively made a bequest of the diya to the 'aqila). There is a discussion about the share of the killer (if the husband is the killer) and whether the bequest to him is valid. The more correct view (al-asahh) is that the entire bequest is effective, with a logical argument to avoid infinite regression. This is a thorough treatment of the intersection of marriage, diya, and bequest law.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by the woman's social status and the dower of her female relatives.
موجبها (mūjibuhā): That which the contract entails, i.e., the consequence; here, the diya.
العاقلة (al-‘āqila): The tribal group or surety responsible for paying diya on behalf of a killer who acted accidentally.
ديَة (diya): Blood money paid for unintentional killing or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman on condition of her being subjected to qisas (hand cut), and she dies from it, what does she receive as dower?
A) The value of her hand.
B) Mahr al-mithl.
C) Nothing.
D) The full diya.

Key Takeaway
When marriage is contracted with an invalid dower, the wife receives mahr al-mithl; in accidental cases, the 'aqila is relieved and the husband's bequest of diya is subject to the one-third rule.

Marriage in Exchange for Injury: Mahr al-Mithl and 'Aqila Liability
Commentary on marriage for injury and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a woman marries in exchange for an injury, derive that the mahr is al-mithl, and explain the effect on the 'aqila and the one-third will limitation.

Core Idea
Marriage for injury is valid, but the mahr is al-mithl, and the 'aqila is relieved proportionally.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi ruling on a marriage contracted in exchange for a hand or injury. The commentary establishes that the marriage is valid but the specified mahr is invalid; instead, the woman receives mahr al-mithl. If the injury was accidental, the 'aqila is relieved of paying the mahr, and any excess above mahr al-mithl is treated as a will from one-third of the estate. The passage also includes a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on the effect of forgiving the hand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the marriage contract and its mahr
The marriage is for the hand or what results from it. The mahr is specified but invalid because it is not a valid subject of property (the hand itself is not wealth).
The hand is a part of the body, not a valid mahr.
2
Determine the effect on validity of the marriage
The marriage is sahih (valid) because the contract itself is sound. However, the invalid mahr defaults to mahr al-mithl (the dower of a woman similar in status).
Analogous to marriage for wine or pig – the specified thing is invalid, but the marriage stands with mahr al-mithl.
3
Analyse the 'aqila's liability
In accidental injury, the 'aqila (relatives liable for diyah) would normally pay diyah. But here, since the diyah becomes the mahr by the contract, if mahr al-mithl equals or exceeds the diyah, the 'aqila is completely relieved. If mahr al-mithl is less, the excess diyah is considered a will from the husband's estate.
The 'aqila's liability is discharged because the obligation transformed into the woman's mahr.
4
Apply the will rule for the excess
If mahr al-mithl is less than the diyah, the excess is a donation (wasiyya) to the 'aqila, but it is only effective up to one-third of the husband's estate. If it exceeds one-third, the 'aqila must pay the surplus to the woman's heirs.
The will to strangers (the 'aqila) is valid but limited to one-third.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that a settlement for the hand alone does not forgive future consequences (e.g., death). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider forgiveness of the hand as forgiveness of whatever may result from it, so the ruling for intentional and accidental injury becomes the same.
The commenter leans towards Abu Hanifa's view when discussing the will correction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مهر المثل ولا شيء عليها ولو خطأ رفع عن العاقلة مهر مثلها ولهم ثلث ما ترك وصية ولو سهم جراحة عمداً وعفا عنه ثم جرحه آخر عمداً فلم يعف حتى مات منهما فلا قود على الثاني. وسئل أبو سلمة عن جماعة كانوا يرمون على كل كلب عقور فأخطأ واحد منهم فأصاب صغيرة فماتت وعرف أن هذا فلان ولكن لم يشهد أحد أنه رماه فلان فصالح صاحب السهم على كرم ثم طلب المصالح رد الصلح قال : إن كان يعلم أن المصالح هو الذي جرحها وأن الصبية ماتت من تلك الجراحة فالصلح ماض، فإن علم أن الجارح صاحب السهم ولكن استغاثت الصغيرة بأبيها فلطمها أبوها فسقطت وماتت ولم يدر أنها ماتت من اللطمة أو من الرمي قال : فإن كان الصلح من الأب بإذن سائر الورثة فالصلح جائز والبدل لسائر الورثة ولا ميراث للأب، وإن كان الميراث بغير إذنهم فالصلح باطل وفي نوادر هشام قال: سألت محمداً عند قلع سن صبي أو حلق رأس امرأة فصالح الجاني أبا الصبي والمرأة على دراهم ونبت الشعر أو السن فأخبر أن أبا حنيفة يرد الدراهم قال : وكذلك أقول، وكذلك قول محمد قال : وكذلك إن كان هذا كسر يده فصالحه عنها ثم جبرت وصحت؟ قال : نم . قلت : فإن زعم صاحب اليد أن يده قد ضعفت وليست كما كانت قال : أمر من ينظر إليها فإنه لا يكاد يخفى. قال رحمه الله : ( وإن تزوجها على اليد وما يحدث منها أو على الجناية فمات منه فلها مهر المثل كما لو تزوجها على خمر أو خنزير وقد تقدم قال رحمه الله : (ولا شيء عليها) لأنه رضي بسقوط القصاص على أنه يصير مهراً وهو لا يصير مهراً فسقط أصلاً فصار كما إذا سقط القصاص بشرط أن لا يصير مالاً فإنه يسقط مجاناً وقد تقدم. قال رحمه الله : (ولو خطأ العاقلة رفع عن مهر مثلها ولهم ثلث ما ترك (وصية لأن التزوج على اليد وما يحدث منها أو على الجناية تزوج على موجبها وموجبها هنا الدية وهي تصلح مهراً فصحت التسمية إلا أنه يقدر مهر مثلها يعتبر من جميع المال لأنه ليس فيه محاباة والمريض لا يجر عليه من التزوج لأنه من الحوائج الأصلية فينفذ قدر مهر مثلها من جميع المال، وما زاد على ذلك الثلث لأنه من تبرع والدية على عاقلتها وقد صارت مهراً فيسقط كلها عنهم إن كان مهر مثلها مثل الدية أو أكثر، ولا يرجع عليهم بشيء لأنهم كانوا يتحملون عنها بسبب جنايتها، فإذا صار ذلك ملكاً لها يسقط عنهم أصلاً فلا يغرمون لها، وإن كان مهر مثلها أقل من الدية سقط أيضاً لأنه وصيته لهم فيصح لأنهم أجانب، وإن كان لا يخرج من الثلث سقط وأدوا الزيادة إلى الولي لأن الوصية لا نفاذ لها إلا من الثلث ثم قيل لا يسقط قدر نصيب القاتل لأن الوصية للقاتل لا تصح والأصح أنه يسقط كله لأنه أوصى لمن تجوز له الوصية فهو كمن أوصى لحي وميت فإن الوصية كلها تكون للحي، ولأنه لو لم يسقط نصيبه لكان ذلك القدر هو الواجب بالقتل فتتحمله العاقلة عنه فينقسم أيضاً فيلزم مثل ذلك عن نصيبه أيضاً ثم هكذا وهكذا إلى أن لا يبقى منه شيء، فلو أبطلنا الوصية في صحته ابتداء لزمنا تصحيحها انتهاء فصححناها ابتداء قصر للمسافة. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : كذلك الجواب فيما إذا تزوجها على اليد أيضاً لأن العفو عن اليد عفو عما يحدث منه عندهما فصار الجواب في الفصلين واحداً. وأقول : في عبارة المصنف احتمال آخر وهو أنه يجوز أن يكون معناها وللعاقلة ثلث ما ترك الميت وصية فيشمل الدية ،وغيرها ولو قال المؤلف ولو العاقلة مهر مثلها والباقي وصية فإن خرج من الثلث سقط وإلا فثلث المال لكان أولى، وقول المؤلف رفع إلى آخره فأفاد أن مهر المثل أقل من الدية كما بيناه.
She gets the mahr al-mithl and nothing upon her. If it was a mistake, the 'aqila is relieved of the mahr of her equal, and they have one third of what he left as a will. And if the arrow of a wound intentionally and he forgave him, then another wounded him intentionally and he did not forgive until he died from both, then no retaliation against the second. Abu Salamah was asked about a group shooting at a rabid dog; one of them missed and hit a young girl who died, and it was known that it was so-and-so, but no one witnessed that so-and-so shot her. The owner of the arrow settled for generosity, then the one who settled sought to return the settlement. He said: If he knows that the settler is the one who wounded her and that the girl died from that wound, the settlement is valid. If he knows that the wounder is the owner of the arrow, but the girl cried out to her father and he slapped her, causing her to fall and die, and it is not known whether she died from the slap or from the shot, he said: If the settlement was from the father with permission of the other heirs, the settlement is valid and the payment is for the other heirs, and the father has no inheritance. If it was without their permission, the settlement is void. In Nawadir Hisham, he said: I asked Muhammad about extracting a boy's tooth or shaving a woman's head; the injurer settled with the boy's father or woman for dirhams, and the hair or tooth grew back. He informed that Abu Hanifa returns the dirhams. He said: I say likewise, and the same is Muhammad's saying. He said: Likewise, if this was a broken hand, and he settled with him about it, then it healed and became sound? He said: yes. I said: If the owner of the hand claims that his hand has weakened and is not as before, he said: Appoint someone to look at it, for it is rarely hidden. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if he marries her in exchange for the hand and what results from it, or for the injury, and she dies from it, she has the mahr al-mithl, just as if he married her for wine or a pig, and it has preceded. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And nothing upon her) because he was satisfied with dropping the retaliation on the condition that it becomes mahr, but it does not become mahr, so it drops completely, just as if the retaliation drops with the condition that it does not become wealth, then it drops for free, and it has preceded. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if it was a mistake, the 'aqila is relieved of the mahr of her equal, and they have one third of what he left as a will) because marrying in exchange for the hand and what results from it, or for the injury, is marrying in exchange for its requisite. Its requisite here is the diyah, which is suitable as mahr, so the specification is valid, except that the mahr al-mithl is estimated and is considered from all the wealth because there is no favoritism, and the sick person is not harmed by marriage because it is from the basic needs, so the amount of her mahr al-mithl is executed from all the wealth. What exceeds that is from one third because it is a donation. The diyah is upon her 'aqila, and it has become mahr, so it drops entirely from them if her mahr al-mithl equals the diyah or more, and they do not pay anything to her because they were bearing it due to her injury. When that becomes her ownership, it drops from them completely, so they do not pay her. If her mahr al-mithl is less than the diyah, it also drops because it is his will for them, and it is valid because they are strangers. If it does not come from one third, it drops and they pay the excess to the guardian because the will is only effective from one third. Then it is said: The share of the killer does not drop because the will for the killer is invalid. The correct view is that it all drops because he willed to someone for whom a will is permissible, so it is like someone who wills to a living person and a dead person: the entire will goes to the living. Also, if his share did not drop, then that amount would be obligatory due to killing, so the 'aqila would bear it for him, then it would divide again, and the same would apply to his share repeatedly until nothing remains. If we invalidate the will in its beginning, we would have to correct it in the end, so we correct it in the beginning to shorten the distance. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, said: The answer is the same regarding marrying in exchange for the hand, because forgiveness for the hand is forgiveness for what results from it according to them, so the answer in both cases is one. I say: In the author's expression, there is another possibility: it could mean that the 'aqila has one third of what the deceased left as a will, which includes the diyah and others. If the author had said: and if the 'aqila [has] her mahr al-mithl and the rest is a will, if it comes from one third it drops, otherwise [they have] one third of the wealth, it would be better. The author's saying 'raised' etc. indicates that the mahr al-mithl is less than the diyah as we explained.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on marriage in exchange for an injury (hand). The commentator explains various scenarios: If the woman dies from the injury, she gets mahr al-mithl. If it was unintentional, the 'aqila (kinsfolk liable for diyah) are relieved of paying the mahr of her equal. The Abu Salamah narration discusses a group shooting at a dog and accidentally killing a child, with complex settlement rules. The key ruling: marrying in exchange for a hand is valid, but the mahr is estimated as al-mithl. Differences between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn are noted regarding the effect of forgiving the hand.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman similar to her in status, not a fixed sum.
عاقلة ('aqila): The group of male relatives (on the father's side) liable for paying diyah in cases of accidental killing or injury.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide or bodily injury.
وصية (wasiyya): A will; a testamentary disposition of up to one-third of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a woman is married in exchange for an intentional injury (hand) and she dies from it, what does she receive?
A) The specified mahr (the hand) as agreed
B) Nothing, because the marriage is invalid
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) The diyah of the hand only

Key Takeaway
A marriage contracted for an invalid mahr (like an injury) is valid, and the wife receives mahr al-mithl, not the specified item.

The Abu Salamah Narration: Settlement and Evidence in Shooting Incidents
Narration of legal cases on settlement (sulh) and evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules of settlement (sulh) in cases of ambiguous causation and identify when a settlement is valid according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A settlement is valid only if the cause of death is known and the settler has authority to settle.

This passage presents a complex case from Abu Salamah about a group shooting at a dog, accidentally killing a girl, and the subsequent settlement. The ruling distinguishes between knowing the wounder and knowing the wounder but with an intervening event. The narration also includes a case about extracting a tooth or shaving hair, where Abu Hanifa rules that if the injury heals, the compensation must be returned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario
The wounder is known (identified shooter), and there is no intervening cause. The settlement is valid because the cause of death is certain and the settler is the actual injurer.
2
Identify the second scenario
The wounder is known, but the father slaps the girl, causing an uncertain cause of death. The settlement by the father is valid only if he had permission from all other heirs; if not, it is void.
The father's inheritance is forfeited as a penalty for acting without permission.
3
Analyse the tooth/hair case from Nawadir
If a person extracts a boy's tooth or shaves a woman's hair, and the tooth/hair grows back perfectly, Abu Hanifa rules that the settlement amount must be returned because the harm is completely remedied.
Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa.
4
Note the rule on weakened limb
If the injured party claims the limb is weakened after healing, an expert should be appointed to assess; the settlement is not automatically returned.
The assessment is based on observable change.

Source Text

يرمون على كل كلب عقور فأخطأ واحد منهم فأصاب صغيرة فماتت وعرف أن هذا فلان ولكن لم يشهد أحد أنه رماه فلان فصالح صاحب السهم على كرم ثم طلب المصالح رد الصلح قال : إن كان يعلم أن المصالح هو الذي جرحها وأن In the tooth extraction case from Nawadir Hisham, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling if the tooth grows back perfectly?

Three Methods for Calculating Muḥābāh in Marriage: The Revolving Share
Detailed comparison of three Hanafi imams' takhreej for muḥābāh in marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi imams' methods for calculating the will amount in a muḥābāh case and explain why they converge on the same result.

Core Idea
The excess dower in illness is a will; three imams' calculations reconcile the revolving share through different paths.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute involving the calculation of muḥābāh (favoritism) in a marriage contract during terminal illness. The three founding imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—each propose a different method (takhreej) for determining the will amount when the sick husband gives a dower above the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) and both parties die. Despite their different computational steps, they arrive at the same final figure of 30 dirhams. This illustrates the flexibility and internal consistency of Hanafi jurisprudence in handling complex inheritance-will intersections.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario and the ruling
State the facts: a sick man marries a woman for 100 dirhams dower, while her proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is 50. He has no other wealth. Both die. The excess (50) is treated as a will from one-third of his estate. Determine the woman's will share.
The will is limited to one-third of the husband's estate after death.
2
Identify the 'revolving share' (sahm da'ir)
The woman inherits from the husband, and the husband inherits from the woman. This reciprocal inheritance creates a portion that 'revolves' back to the husband, requiring careful subtraction to avoid double counting.
The term 'revolving share' is unique to this calculation.
3
Walk through Abu Hanifa's method
Start with the husband's total estate: the excess (50) plus what he inherits from her (25) = 75. Divide 75 into shares: treat the woman's share as 1/3? Actually, the method uses a 3-share division, then corrects for the revolving portion. Follow the text's steps: 3 shares → 6 shares, subtract the revolving share, arrive at 30 for the woman.
Abu Hanifa uses a base of 75 and a fractional manipulation.
4
Compare with Abu Yusuf's method
Start with the favoritism amount (50) and give the woman one-third of that (16.66). Then add the inheritance from her (his half of her estate including her proper dower) and apply a similar share correction. His steps yield the same 30.
Abu Yusuf separates the will from the inheritance initially.
5
Compare with Muhammad's method
Start with the same 16.66, add the proper dower (50) to get 66.66, then divide into 2 shares (husband's inheritance share and woman's will share). After adjusting for the fraction, the result is again 30.
Muhammad uses a simpler 2-share method without explicitly introducing the revolving share.
6
Verify and reflect
Confirm that all three methods yield 30 dirhams. Reflect on the unity of legal principle despite differing computational paths.
This shows the depth of Hanafi methodology: different takhreej can lead to the same hukm.

He (may God have mercy on him) said: (And his favoritism) meaning in his illness is a will considered from the third. It is said in al-Muhit: Favoritism in illness is a will. He generalized favoritism to include if it is in marriage or... its origin is that a sale: the will is a valid inheritance contract because the benefits of the vulva at entry are valuable. And if a sick man marries a woman for a hundred dirhams with no other wealth, and her proper dower is fifty dirhams, then the woman dies, then the husband dies, her will is thirty-three and one-third dirhams. The extraction: the husband's property due to favoritism is fifty, and what he inherits from her is half her proper dower, twenty-five, so the husband's wealth becomes seventy-five. It is divided into three shares: one share for the woman, half of it returns to the husband by inheritance, so it breaks and is multiplied to six: two shares for the woman, one share returns to the husband... (continued) ... So her will becomes thirty.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on favoritism (muḥābāh) in a marriage contract during terminal illness. The author states that according to al-Muḥīṭ, muḥābāh in illness is a will. He then presents a case: a sick man marries a woman for a dower of 100 dirhams, while her proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is 50; he has no other wealth. After both die, the calculation of her will share is done in three different ways by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Each method accounts for the 'revolving share' (sahm da'ir) that returns from the woman's inheritance to the husband. The passage details each imam's takhreej, showing how they arrive at the same final amount of 30 dirhams for the woman's will despite different intermediate steps. This illustrates the principle that the effective cause (ʿilla) for treating muḥābāh as a will is the excess over the proper dower, and the calculation must avoid double counting.

Key Terms
محاباة (muḥābāh): Favoritism or excessive dower; specifically, giving more than the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) in a marriage contract during illness.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower; the amount typically given to a woman of her status.
السهم الدائر (al-sahm al-da'ir): The revolving share; a portion that returns to one party from another through inheritance, requiring careful subtraction.
تخريج (takhreej): Extraction or method of deriving the legal ruling or mathematical calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage
