Will for Manumission of Parents and Brother: Abu Hanifa vs Muhammad
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on will for manumitting parents and brother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and Muhammad al-Shaybani's rulings on a will to manumit parents and a brother, and state the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) regarding the brother's obligation to work (sa'y).

Core Idea
A will for a non-heir is more freely permitted; this affects distribution of the one-third and the obligation of sa'y.

A terminally ill man purchases his parents and brother with the intention of freeing them after his death. The will is limited to one-third of his estate, leading to a dispute: should the one-third be shared among the three, or given entirely to the brother who does not inherit? This lesson examines the positions of two great Hanafi imams, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and highlights how inheritance principles shape the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A man in his death illness buys his parents and his brother for equal sums (total 3000 dirhams) with the intention of manumitting them. Their values are equal. The will is subject to the one-third rule (limiting bequests to one-third of the estate after debts and funeral expenses).
The one-third rule applies to all bequests, including wills for manumission.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position
According to the analogy of Abu Hanifa's statement, the will for manumission is valid for the mother and the brother, and the one-third is distributed between them. The father gets what remains (i.e., not covered by the third). Consequently, the mother and brother must each work (sa'y) for half their value to compensate the heirs for the excess over the third.
Abu Hanifa treats the mother and brother as heirs (the mother inherits, the brother does not when father is present) but still allocates the will share to both.
3
Present Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the entire will is valid for the brother alone, because the brother does not inherit when manumitted along with the parents (the father and mother block his inheritance). Thus his manumission does not affect the heirs' shares. The mother gets no part of the will; she inherits normally alongside the father, and she must work for any amount exceeding her inheritance share.
Muhammad's ruling gives the brother full freedom without sa'y.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that under Abu Hanifa, the brother must work for half his value; under Muhammad, the brother is fully free without any work obligation. The mother also has a different obligation: in Abu Hanifa's view, she works for half; in Muhammad's, she works only if her inheritance share is less than the excess.
The dispute hinges on whether the brother is considered an heir in this context.
5
Note the underlying principle
The principle at play is that a will for a non-heir is more freely permitted (i.e., can exceed the one-third if the heirs consent, but here it is within the third). Muhammad treats the brother as a non-heir, so the will can be fully given to him. Abu Hanifa treats the brother as potentially affected by the will, sharing it with the mother.
This illustrates how inheritance status influences the distribution of bequests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجل اشترى أبويه وأخاه في مرضه بثلاثة آلاف درهم وقيمتهم سواء ففي قياس قول أبي حنيفة تجوز الوصية بالعتق للأم والأخ والثلث بينهما وللأب ما بقي وتسعى الأم في نصف قيمتها والأخ في نصف قيمته. وقال محمد: الوصية كلها للأخ جائزة لأنه لا يرث بأن يعتق مع الأبوين ولا وصية للأم ولها الميراث مع الأب وتسعى فيما زاد على حصتها.
A man bought his parents and his brother in his illness for three thousand dirhams and their value is equal. According to the analogy of Abu Hanifa's statement, the will for manumission is valid for the mother and the brother, and the third is between them, and for the father what remains, and the mother must work for half her value and the brother for half his value. And Muhammad said: the entire will is valid for the brother, because he does not inherit when manumitted with the parents, and there is no will for the mother, and she inherits with the father, and she must work for what exceeds her share.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a man who, in his terminal illness, purchases his parents and his brother with three thousand dirhams (equal value for each) with the intention of manumitting them. The will for manumission is subject to the one-third rule. According to the position attributed to Abu Hanifa, the will is valid for the mother and the brother (who both get a share of the third), and the father gets what remains after the third is exhausted. Consequently, the mother and brother must work (sa'y) for half their value to compensate the heirs for the excess over the third. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the entire will is valid for the brother alone because the brother does not inherit when manumitted along with the parents (since he is not an heir), so his manumission does not affect the heirs' shares; the mother gets no will but inherits normally, and she must work for the amount exceeding her share. This illustrates the principle that a will for a non-heir is more freely permitted.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'ā): The obligation of a partially manumitted slave to work to earn the remaining portion of his value for the owner's heirs.
الوصية بالعتق (al-wasiyyah bil-'itq): A will that a slave be manumitted after the testator's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa in this case, what happens to the mother after the will is executed?
A) She is fully free without payment
B) She must work for half her value
C) She inherits nothing
D) The will is invalid for her

Key Takeaway
The distribution of a will for manumission within the one-third depends on whether the beneficiary is an heir; a non-heir may receive the full third, but the school's relied-upon position is more cautious.

Combined Bequest of Manumission and Money: Two Fatwas from Al-Fatawa
Ruling on combined will for manumission and money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid bequest of manumission combined with money and apply the rulings from the fatwas to similar cases.

Core Idea
An executor must follow the testator's conditions exactly; a slave cannot be manumitted early even with consent, and surplus gifts revert to the estate.

This lesson explores two fatwas from al-Fatawa that clarify the boundaries of a combined bequest of manumission and money. In the first, the testator delays manumission until his son matures; the executor cannot manumit earlier even if the slave consents. In the second, when slaves already have goods from the testator, a bequest of additional money does not entitle them to luxury items beyond basic covering. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that the testator's conditions are binding and that bequests are limited to the specified scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the source text and distinguish the first fatwa (Abu al-Qasim's case: will for manumission at a future time plus a gift, slave commits tort) from the second (Abu Bakr's case: will for manumission of two slaves plus gift, slaves already have goods).
The first scenario includes a tort leading to the slave being handed over.
2
Extract the core ruling for each
From the first: the executor cannot manumit before the appointed time. From the second: the slaves only get what covers their bodies from the pre-existing goods, not the full gift.
The ruling on tort: if the slave is surrendered, the bequest of manumission is void; if ransomed, the text is unclear.
3
Analyze the conditions they establish
The first establishes condition of time: executor must adhere to the testator's timeline. The second establishes condition of need: the bequest of money/goods is limited to essential covering if the slaves already have sufficient clothing.
The condition of time is explicit (لا يجوز قبل الوقت). The condition of need is inferred from the ruling.
4
Apply to hypothetical scenarios
Test the rulings: if a testator says 'free my slave after my death and give him 100 dirhams', but the slave already has 50 dirhams, can he take the full 100? The second fatwa suggests he only gets enough to cover basic needs. If the testator says 'free him when he turns 30', but the slave turns 30 earlier, can the executor free him early? He must wait.
The Hanafi school strictly follows the testator's wording in condition (amr bi al-shart).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا إذا أوصى له بالعتق فقط، فلو أوصى له بالعتق وبالمال قال في الفتاوى: سأل أبو القاسم عمن أوصى إلى رجل فقال إذا بلغ ولدي فأعتق عبدي هذا وأعطه عبده فمات فجنى ودفع بطلت وإن فدى لا وبثلثه لزيد وترك عبداً فادعى زيد عتقه في العتق من ا. مائتي درهم والعبد مفسد وهو في تعب منه فرضي العبد أن يعتق في الحال ولا يطلب صلته قال : لا يجوز عتق الوصي قبل الوقت الذي أقر به الموصي وسأل أبو بكر عمن أوصى بعتق عبديه وأوصى لهم بصلة وللعبيد متاع وكسوة كسا لهم صاحبهم ومتاع وهبة لهم من غير المولى قال : لا يكون للعبيد من المتاع إلا ما يواري جسدهم.
This applies if he bequeathed only manumission. But if he bequeathed both manumission and money, it is stated in al-Fatawa: Abu al-Qasim asked concerning one who made a will to a man, saying: when my son reaches maturity, manumit this slave of mine and give him his slave. Then he died, and the slave committed a tort and was handed over, so it is void, and if he ransomed, no. And with his third for Zayd, and he left a slave, and Zayd claimed his manumission in the manumission from ... two hundred dirhams, and the slave is corrupt and he is tired of him, so the slave agreed to be manumitted immediately and not to ask for his gift. He said: it is not permissible for the executor to manumit before the time appointed by the testator. And Abu Bakr asked concerning one who bequeathed manumission of his two slaves and bequeathed them a gift, and the slaves have goods and clothing given to them by their owner, and a gift to them from someone other than the master. He said: the slaves do not get from the goods except what covers their bodies.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage contains two fatwas from al-Fatawa related to combined bequests of manumission and money. The first case involves a testator who appoints an executor to manumit a specific slave when the son reaches maturity, and also to give him another slave. After the testator's death, the slave commits a tort (جناية) and is handed over as compensation. The ruling: the will for manumission is void because the slave is no longer in the estate. If the executor ransoms the slave, the will remains? The text is unclear but seems to say 'no'. Additionally, the testator had bequeathed a third to Zayd, and a slave is claimed by Zayd. The slave agrees to immediate manumission without asking for the gift. The answer: the executor cannot manumit before the appointed time (when the son matures). The second fatwa: if a testator bequeaths manumission of two slaves and gives them a gift (صلة), and the slaves already have some goods and clothing from the testator and a gift from someone else, the slaves only get what covers their bodies (essentials), not the excess, because the gift is for manumission only.

Key Terms
وصي (waṣī): Executor of a will; the person appointed to carry out the testator's instructions.
صلة (ṣilah): A gift or grant; here, a bequest of money or goods to the slaves along with manumission.
عتق (‘itq): Manumission; freeing a slave.
جناية (jināyah): Tort; a wrongful act causing harm, here committed by the slave.
وقت (waqt): Time; the appointed time for manumission set by the testator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Before the testator's death
B) Before the appointed time set by the testator
C) If the slave is corrupt
D) If the slave asks for freedom

Key Takeaway
An executor must strictly adhere to the testator's conditions regarding timing and scope; early manumission and excess gifts beyond essential covering are invalid.

Invalidity of Premature Manumission by an Executor
Fatwa on premature manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an executor cannot free a slave before the testator's specified condition is met and explain the legal basis.

Core Idea
An executor must strictly follow the testator's condition; premature manumission is invalid.

This lesson examines a specific fatwa from Abu al-Qasim regarding an executor who frees a slave before the condition set by the testator (the child's maturity). Understanding this ruling clarifies the strict binding nature of conditions in Hanafi bequest law and the limited authority of an executor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the first part of the passage: a testator instructs his executor to free a slave and give him money when the testator's child reaches maturity. The slave is present and agrees to be freed immediately.
2
Spot the condition
The testator attached a clear condition: the freeing must happen upon the child's maturity. This condition is binding on the executor.
3
Understand the ruling
The fatwa rules that the executor cannot free the slave before the condition is fulfilled. The slave's consent does not override the testator's stipulation.
4
Recognize the legal principle
Hanafi law holds that an executor (wasi) must act precisely within the testator's instructions. Any deviation invalidates the act unless there is a necessity (which is absent here).
This principle is rooted in the sanctity of the testator's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوى سأل أبو القاسم عمن أوصى إلى رجل فقال إذا أدرك ولدي فأعتق عبدي هذا وأعطه مائتي درهم والعبد معه وهو في لعب منه فرضي العبد أن يعتق في الحال ولا يطلب منه شيئاً قال : لا يجوز عتق العبد قبل الوقت الذي أقر به الوصي. وسأل أبو بكر عمن أوصى بعتق عبده وأوصى له بصلة وللعبد متاع وكسوة من سيده وهبة وهبها له غير المولى قال : لا يكون للعبد من ذلك المتاع إلا ما يواري عورته
And in al-Fatawa: Abu al-Qasim asked about one who appointed an executor and said: 'When my child reaches maturity, free this slave of mine and give him two hundred dirhams.' The slave is with the executor and plays with him, and the slave agreed to be freed immediately without asking for anything. He said: 'The freeing of the slave before the time appointed by the executor is not permissible.' And Abu Bakr asked about one who bequeathed to free his slave and bequeathed him a gift, and the slave also has belongings and clothing from his master and a gift given to him by someone other than the master. He said: 'The slave does not get from those belongings except what covers his 'awrah.'
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage presents two fatwa rulings from early Hanafi scholars. The first, from Abu al-Qasim, concerns an executor who was instructed to free a slave when the testator's child reaches maturity. The slave agrees to be freed immediately, but the ruling is that this is not permissible because the executor must adhere to the testator's condition. The slave cannot waive the condition; the freedom is conditional upon the child's maturity. The second fatwa, from Abu Bakr, deals with a bequest that includes freeing the slave and giving him a gift, but the slave also has his own belongings and clothing from the master, as well as gifts from others. The ruling is that from all these items, the slave only takes what is necessary to cover his ‘awrah (the parts of the body that must be concealed). The rest belongs to the master's estate. This limits the slave's entitlement to only a modest amount of clothing, preventing him from taking excessive wealth from the bequest.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): Executor of a will: the person appointed to carry out the testator's instructions.
عتق ('itq): Manumission: freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is valid if the slave consents.
B) It is not permissible (la yajuz).
C) It is valid if the executor pays compensation.
D) It is valid if the testator's child approves.

Key Takeaway
An executor must strictly adhere to the testator's conditional terms; premature action invalidates the bequest, even with the beneficiary's consent.

Slave's Entitlement to Bequeathed Clothing
Fatwa on slave's clothing entitlement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine how much clothing a slave receives under a bequest of 'kiswah' according to Hanafi law and explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
A slave's bequest of clothing is limited only to what covers the 'awrah; excess belongs to the estate.

This lesson examines the second fatwa from Abu Bakr regarding the extent of a slave's entitlement to clothing when the testator bequeathed 'kiswah' (clothing). The ruling clarifies that such bequests are interpreted minimally to prevent waste of the estate and ensure the testator's intention is fulfilled without excessive depletion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A testator bequeaths his slave a gift (silah) and the slave also has personal belongings and clothing from the master, plus gifts from others. The bequest includes freeing the slave and giving him a silah.
2
Understand the question
The question is: what portion of the clothing (and other items) does the slave get from the bequest? The fatwa specifies that from these belongings, the slave only takes what covers his 'awrah.
3
Apply the 'awrah principle
The clothes are limited to the minimum necessary to cover the 'awrah. Anything beyond that belongs to the estate, as the bequest is interpreted restrictively.
4
Recognize the legal reasoning
Hanafi law interprets vague bequests (like 'clothing') in the most minimal sense to balance the testator's generosity with the rights of heirs. Excess is not given to the slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوى سأل أبو القاسم عمن أوصى إلى رجل فقال إذا أدرك ولدي فأعتق عبدي هذا وأعطه مائتي درهم والعبد معه وهو في لعب منه فرضي العبد أن يعتق في الحال ولا يطلب منه شيئاً قال : لا يجوز عتق العبد قبل الوقت الذي أقر به الوصي. وسأل أبو بكر عمن أوصى بعتق عبده وأوصى له بصلة وللعبد متاع وكسوة من سيده وهبة وهبها له غير المولى قال : لا يكون للعبد من ذلك المتاع إلا ما يواري عورته
And in al-Fatawa: Abu al-Qasim asked about one who appointed an executor and said: 'When my child reaches maturity, free this slave of mine and give him two hundred dirhams.' The slave is with the executor and plays with him, and the slave agreed to be freed immediately without asking for anything. He said: 'The freeing of the slave before the time appointed by the executor is not permissible.' And Abu Bakr asked about one who bequeathed to free his slave and bequeathed him a gift, and the slave also has belongings and clothing from his master and a gift given to him by someone other than the master. He said: 'The slave does not get from those belongings except what covers his 'awrah.'
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage presents two fatwa rulings from early Hanafi scholars. The first, from Abu al-Qasim, concerns an executor who was instructed to free a slave when the testator's child reaches maturity. The slave agrees to be freed immediately, but the ruling is that this is not permissible because the executor must adhere to the testator's condition. The slave cannot waive the condition; the freedom is conditional upon the child's maturity. The second fatwa, from Abu Bakr, deals with a bequest that includes freeing the slave and giving him a gift, but the slave also has his own belongings and clothing from the master, as well as gifts from others. The ruling is that from all these items, the slave only takes what is necessary to cover his ‘awrah (the parts of the body that must be concealed). The rest belongs to the master's estate. This limits the slave's entitlement to only a modest amount of clothing, preventing him from taking excessive wealth from the bequest.

Key Terms
كسوة (kiswah): Clothing provided to a slave as part of a bequest or gift.
عورة ('awrah): The parts of the body that must be covered in front of non-mahram. For a slave, the 'awrah is the same as for a free person in terms of coverage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Bakr's fatwa, what does the slave receive from the bequeathed clothing?
A) All clothing from the master.
B) Clothing that covers his 'awrah only.
C) Half of the clothing.
D) Nothing, because the bequest is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A vague bequest of clothing to a slave is interpreted minimally as only enough to cover the 'awrah; surplus remains in the estate.

Father's Use of Minor's Property: Dower, Purchase, and Debt
Rulings on father's transactions with minor's property and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on a father's marriage using his minor son's slave as dower and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A father may use minor's property for his own benefit, but he becomes a guarantor and must compensate if the minor suffers loss.

This passage presents several cases where a father transacts with his minor child's property for his own purposes. The central tension is between the father's guardianship and the minor's right to property. The Hanafi school allows such transactions under istihsan but imposes liability on the father to protect the minor. The key ikhtilaf is between Abu Hanifa, who validates the transaction with compensation, and Abu Yusuf, who invalidates it altogether.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary transaction
The first case is a father marrying a woman using his minor son's slave girl as dower. State the act and the parties involved.
The dower (mahr) must be validly owned by the husband; here the father uses the son's property.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and the legal consequence
According to Abu Hanifa, the dower is initially valid but once the father delivers the slave, he becomes a transgressor (mut'addin) and must pay the value to the son.
The father's guarantee (daman) is the compensation for using the minor's property.
3
State Abu Yusuf's ruling and the practical difference
Abu Yusuf holds that the dower is invalid from the start; the father must pay the wife her dower directly.
This changes who receives compensation: under Abu Hanifa, the son is compensated; under Abu Yusuf, the wife is.
4
Apply the same analytical pattern to other cases
The passage extends to purchasing a slave for an incapacitated person, selling minor's property for own debt, and pledging minor's property. In each, note whether the transaction is valid and who bears liability.
The pattern: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow with guarantee; Abu Yusuf disallows.
5
Identify the role of istihsan
In the case of buying a slave for the incapacitated, qiyas would make the father liable, but istihsan makes the transaction valid. Explain how istihsan overrides strict analogy.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi principle that considers necessity and public interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى بشر عن أبي يوسف : رجل تزوج امرأة على أمة لابنه الصغير فهو جائز، وإذا أسلم الأمة يصير متعدياً ويضمن قيمة الأمة في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي قول أبي يوسف لا يصح إمهار الأمة ويكون على الأب قيمتها للزوجة. وفي الذخيرة: اشترى الأب قريب الصبي أو المعتوه لا يجوز على الصبي والمعتوه ويجوز على الأب، ولو اشترى للمعتوه أمة كان استولدها بحكم النكاح يلزم الأب قياساً، وفي الاستحسان يجوز، وهذا القياس والاستحسان على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعلى قول أبي يوسف لا يجوز أصلاً، فهذه المسألة على أن الأب إذا باع مال الصغير بدين نفسه من رب الدين بمثل ما عليه من الدين على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد يجوز ويصير الثمن قصاصاً بدينه ويصير هو ضامناً للصغير خلافاً لأبي يوسف وأجمعوا على أن الأب إذا أراد أن يوفي دينه من مال الصغير ليس له ذلك ؛ هكذا ذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي في شرحه أن الأب لا يملك قضاء دین مال الصبي. وذكر القاضي الإمام صدر الإسلام في شرح كتاب الرهن أنه يجوز، ويحتمل أن يكون في المسألة روايتان. وإذا صح رهن الأب متاع الصغير بدين نفسه عندهما فهلك الرهن في يد المرتهن هلك بما فيه ويضمن الأب للصغير قيمة الرهن إن كانت القيمة مثل الدين أو أقل، أما إذا كانت القيمة أكثر من الثلث يضمن مقدار الدين ولا يضمن الزيادة. وذكر شمس الأئمة في شرح كتاب الرهن أن للأب أن يستقرض مال ولده لنفسه. وذكر شيخ الإسلام في شرحه أنه ليس له ذلك. وذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني: روى الحسن عن أبي يوسف عن أبي حنيفة أن الأب ينفق من مال ابنه على نفسه.
And Bishr narrated from Abu Yusuf: A man married a woman with a slave girl belonging to his minor son as dower, so it is permissible. And if he hands over the slave girl, he becomes a transgressor and guarantees the value of the slave girl according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, the dowering of the slave girl is not valid, and the father owes her value to the wife. And in al-Dhakhira: The father buys a relative of the minor or the incapacitated, it is not valid on the minor or incapacitated, and it is valid on the father. And if he bought for the incapacitated a slave woman and then had children with her by virtue of marriage, by qiyas it is binding on the father, and by istihsan it is permissible. This qiyas and istihsan are according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf it is not valid at all. So this issue is that if the father sells the property of the minor for his own debt to the creditor for the equivalent of what he owes in debt, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad it is permissible, and the price becomes a set-off for his debt, and he becomes a guarantor for the minor, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And they are agreed that if the father wants to pay his debt from the property of the minor, he does not have that right. Thus Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in his commentary that the father does not have the right to pay his debt from the minor's wealth. And Qadi Imam Sadr al-Islam mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Rahn that it is permissible, and it is possible that there are two narrations on the issue. And if the father's pledge of the minor's property for his own debt is valid according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and then the pledge is destroyed in the hand of the pledgee, it is destroyed including its value, and the father guarantees the minor the value of the pledge if the value equals the debt or is less. But if the value is more than the debt, he guarantees the amount of the debt and does not guarantee the excess. And Shams al-Aimma mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Rahn that the father may borrow from his child's wealth for himself. And Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in his commentary that he does not have that right. And Shams al-Aimma al-Halwani mentioned: al-Hasan narrated from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa that the father may spend from his son's wealth on himself.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage brings together several rulings on the father's use of the minor's property for his own purposes. The first case: a father marries using his minor son's slave girl as dower. Abu Hanifa says it is initially valid but if he delivers her, he becomes a transgressor and must pay her value to the son. Abu Yusuf says the dower is invalid outright, and the father must pay the wife her dower. This is a clear ikhtilaf between the two imams. The second case: buying a relative of the minor is valid on the father, not on the minor. For buying a slave woman for an incapacitated (ma'tuh) and then having children with her, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say by qiyas it is binding on the father (i.e., he is liable), but by istihsan it is permissible (i.e., the children are legitimate and the slave woman's status is regularized). Abu Yusuf says it is not valid at all. The third case: father sells minor's property to pay his own debt. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow it with set-off, making him guarantor for the minor. Abu Yusuf disagrees. There is a consensus that the father cannot simply use minor's property to pay his debt without a transaction. Sarakhsi and Sadr al-Islam differ on whether he can pay his debt directly; possibly two narrations. The passage then discusses pledging minor's property for the father's debt: if destroyed, father guarantees value up to the debt. Finally, a dispute whether the father can borrow from the minor's wealth: Shams al-Aimma allows it, Shaykh al-Islam forbids it. Al-Halwani narrates from Hasan ibn Ziyad that the father can spend on himself from the son's wealth.

Key Terms
إمهار (imhar): Giving something as dower (mahr) in a marriage contract.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding qiyas; here it allows a transaction that would otherwise be invalid by analogy.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor or one who is liable to compensate for loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the consequence for a father who uses his minor son's slave girl as dower and delivers her?
A) The marriage is invalid and the father must pay the wife.
B) The father becomes a transgressor and guarantees the slave's value to the son.
C) The father is not liable because he is the guardian.
D) The son must ratify the marriage.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows a father to use his minor's property but imposes a guarantee to protect the minor's rights, with Abu Hanifa generally more permissive than Abu Yusuf.

Gender Determination of the Khuntha by Urination: Abu Hanifah vs. the Sahibayn
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on gender determination by urination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on gender determination by urination and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on the relevance of quantity.

Core Idea
Only the first urination determines the khuntha's gender; quantity is irrelevant.

This passage addresses a unique fiqh scenario: determining the gender of a person with ambiguous genitalia (khuntha). The ruling relies on a pre-Islamic practice confirmed by the Shari'ah. Within the Hanafi school, a dispute arises: should quantity matter when both organs urinate simultaneously? We will explore Abu Hanifah's position and the counter-argument by his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The khuntha urinates from both organs. What is the legal method to assign gender? The text first rules that the organ that urinates first determines gender; if simultaneous, the person is ambiguous (mushkil).
This is the base ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
State Abu Hanifah's ruling
Abu Hanifah holds that only precedence matters. If both urinate at the same time, the khuntha remains ambiguous. Quantity of urine is irrelevant.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Contrast with the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that if the urination is simultaneous, gender is determined by the organ that produces more urine, based on the principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Evaluate the proofs
Abu Hanifah argues that the exit itself is the complete sign; quantity is like measuring urine, which is repugnant. The Sahibayn analogize to the majority rule. Which proof is stronger based on the school's method?
The author (al-Marghinani) sides with Abu Hanifah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن قاضياً . العرب في الجاهلية رفع عليه هذه الواقعة فجعل يقول هو ذكر وامرأة فاستبعد قوله ذلك فتحير ودخل فجعل يتقلب على فراشه ولا يأخذه النوم لتحيره وكانت له بنت تغمز رجله فسألته عن ذكره فأخبرها بذلك فقالت : دع واتبع الحكم المبال فخرج إلى قومه فحكى لهم ذلك فاستحسنوا فعرف بذلك أن هذا الحكم كان في الجاهلية فأقره الشرع، ولأن البول من أي عضو كان فهو دليل على أنه هو والأصلي الصحيح والآخر بمنزلة العيب. وذلك إنما يقع به الولادة لأن منفعة تلك الآلة خروج البول وذلك عند انفصاله ذلك من المنافع يحدث بعده فعلم بذلك من أمه وما سوى هو الأصل. قال رحمه الله : (فإن بال منهما فالحكم للأسبق لأنه دليل على أنه العضو الأصلي، ولأنه كما خرج البول حكم بموجبه . لأنه علامة تامة فلا يتغير بعد ذلك بخروج البول من الآلة الأخرى. قال رحمه الله: (فإن استويا) أي في السبق فمشكل لعدم المرجح . رحمه الله : ( ولا عبرة بالكثرة) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا ينسب إلى أكثرهما بولاً لأنه قال يدل على أنه العضو الأصلي ولأن للأكثر حكم الكل في أصول الشرع فيترجح بالكثرة. وله أن كثرة ما يخرج ليس بدليل على الآلة لأن ذلك لاتساع المخرج وضيقه لا لأنه هو العضو الأصلي، ولأن نفس الخروج دليل بنفسه فالكثرة لا يقع بها الترجيح عند المعارضة كالشاهدين والأربعة، وقد استقبح أبو حنيفة اعتبار ذلك فقال : هل رأيت قاضياً يكيل البول بالأواقي؟
A judge among the Arabs in the Jahiliyyah was presented with this case and he kept saying 'he is a male and female,' so his statement was considered unlikely. He was confused and entered (his house), tossing on his bed, unable to sleep due to confusion. He had a daughter who massaged his leg; she asked him about his story, and he told her. She said: 'Leave it and follow the ruling of urination.' So he went out to his people and narrated that to them, and they approved it. Thus it became known that this ruling existed in Jahiliyyah and the Law confirmed it. And because urine from whichever organ is evidence that that is the [true] organ, and the other is like a defect. That is because the benefit of that organ is the exit of urine, and that occurs when it separates [from the body], and so it is known from that that it is the original. And what is other than it is the original. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'If he urinates from both, the ruling is for the earlier [organ] because it is evidence that it is the original organ, and because as soon as the urine exits, it is ruled accordingly; it is a complete sign, so it does not change afterward by the exit of urine from the other organ.' He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'If they are equal' i.e., in precedence, then it is ambiguous due to the lack of a preponderating factor. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And no consideration is given to quantity.' This is according to Abu Hanifah. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: he is attributed to the one from which he urinates more, because he said it indicates that it is the original organ, and because the majority has the ruling of the whole in the principles of the Law, so preponderance is given by quantity. And his (Abu Hanifah's) proof is that the quantity of what exits is not evidence for the organ, because that is due to the width or narrowness of the outlet, not because it is the original organ; and because the exit itself is evidence by itself, so quantity does not give preponderance in case of conflict, like two witnesses and four. And Abu Hanifah considered that [quantity] to be repugnant, saying: 'Have you seen a judge measuring urine by ounces?'
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of determining the gender of a khuntha (hermaphrodite) when both organs function. The author first presents the ruling that if both organs produce urine, the one that urinates first determines the gender. This is based on the practice of the pre-Islamic Arabs, which was confirmed by the Prophet (peace be upon him) and Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). The reasoning is that the first urination indicates the original organ; the other is superfluous. If both urinate simultaneously, the khuntha is considered ambiguous (mushkil). Then the author discusses a point of disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifah and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Hanifah holds that the quantity of urine is irrelevant—only precedence matters. His position is that the exit itself is the sign, not the amount; comparing it to witnesses where number does not affect credibility. The Sahibayn argue that if they are equal in time, then the greater quantity indicates the true organ, based on the principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole. Abu Hanifah finds this absurd, famously asking if a judge would measure urine in ounces. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifah, as the text indicates by mentioning his disapproval. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah via the commentary.

Key Terms
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A person who possesses both male and female genitalia or ambiguous genitalia.
الأسبق (al-asbaq): The organ that urinates first.
مشكل (mushkil): Ambiguous; gender cannot be determined due to equal signs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a khuntha urinates from both organs at the same time, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifah?
A) Gender is determined by which organ produces more urine.
B) The khuntha is considered male because the male organ is original.
C) The khuntha is ambiguous (mushkil) until further signs appear.
D) The khuntha is considered female because the female organ is more common.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the gender of a khuntha is determined by the first urination; simultaneous urination renders the person ambiguous, and quantity of urine is irrelevant.

Determining Gender of a Khuntha by Puberty Signs
Ruling on gender determination via puberty signs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the signs of puberty that determine the gender of a khuntha and apply them to classify a case as male, female, or ambiguous.

Core Idea
Puberty signs like beard (male) and breasts (female) conclusively determine the gender of a khuntha.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq gives clear physical signs for determining the gender of a person born with ambiguous genitalia (khuntha). These signs are practical and legally decisive for applying rules of marriage, inheritance, and other areas of fiqh. We will examine each sign and how to handle contradictory cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three signs of male puberty
The text lists beard growth, intercourse with women (as a male), and wet dream from the male organ. If any of these appear, the person is conclusively male.
These are external and observable signs.
2
Identify the three signs of female puberty
Breast development, milk production, or ability to be penetrated (i.e., functioning female organ) indicate female gender.
Each sign alone is sufficient.
3
Handle cases with no or contradictory signs
If no sign appears or signs conflict (e.g., beard and breasts), the status remains ambiguous (mushkil). The minority rib-counting view is not relied upon.
Ambiguous cases require different rules (e.g., inheritance as half-male half-female).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (إن بلغ وخرجت له لحية أو وصل إلى النساء فرجل وكذا إذا احتلم من الذكر لأن هذه علامة الذكر . قال رحمه الله : (وإن ظهر له ثدي أو لبن أو أمكن وطؤه فامرأة) لأن هذه من علامات النساء. قال رحمه الله : ( وإن لم تظهر له علامة أو تعارضت فمشكل) لعدم ما يوجب الترجيح. وعن الحسن أنه يعد أضلاعه فإن أضلاع الرجل تزيد عن أضلاع المرأة بواحد .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'If he reaches puberty and grows a beard, or has intercourse with women, then he is a man; likewise if he has a wet dream from the male organ, because these are signs of the male.' He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if a breast appears, or milk, or it is possible for him to be penetrated, then she is a woman, because these are signs of women.' He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if no sign appears, or signs are contradictory, then he/she is ambiguous, due to the lack of a preponderating factor.' And it is narrated from al-Hasan that his ribs should be counted, for the ribs of a male exceed those of a female by one.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage lists the puberty signs that definitively determine the gender of a khuntha. If the person grows a beard, has intercourse with women (as a male), or experiences a wet dream from the male organ, he is conclusively male. If breasts develop, milk is produced, or the person is capable of being penetrated (i.e., the female organ is functional), then the person is female. If no such sign appears, or if contradictory signs appear (e.g., both beard and breasts), the status remains ambiguous (mushkil). The author also mentions a minority opinion from al-Hasan al-Basri that counting ribs can determine gender, but this is not the relied-upon view. These signs are practical and easy to observe, and they override the earlier urination-based determination. The authority weight is from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
البلوغ (al-bulugh): Reaching puberty, which triggers these signs.
اللحية (al-lihyah): Beard, a sign of male puberty.
الثدي (al-thady): Breast development, a sign of female puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a sign that the khuntha is male?
A) Development of breasts.
B) Production of milk.
C) Growth of a beard.
D) Ability to be penetrated.

Key Takeaway
The gender of a khuntha after puberty is determined by specific observable signs; without them or with conflicting signs, the status remains ambiguous.

Marriage of a Khuntha to a Woman: Suspension and Inheritance
Ruling on marriage suspension for a khuntha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marriage of a khuntha to a woman and explain why inheritance is suspended until gender clarity.

Core Idea
A khuntha's marriage is valid but suspended — no inheritance until gender becomes clear.

When a father marries his khuntha child to a woman before puberty, the marriage is not invalid but suspended. This lesson examines the ruling and its practical consequence for inheritance and the one-year respite for consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status
The passage states the marriage is 'mawquf' (suspended), not batil or fasid. Recognize this as a unique Hanafi category.
2
Explain the inheritance rule
Inheritance is a consequence of a valid effective marriage, not a suspended one. Therefore, spouses do not inherit until gender is clear.
3
Apply the clarity condition
If male signs appear after puberty, the marriage becomes valid. If not consummated, a one-year respite is given.
This matches the standard rule for any husband who delays consummation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في مسائل النكاح لو زوج الأب هذا الخنثى امرأة قبل بلوغه أو زوجة فالنكاح موقوف لا يفسد ولا يبطل ولا يتوارثان حتى يستبين أمر الخنثى لأن التوارث حكم النكاح النافذ لا حكم النكاح الموقوف، فإن زوجه الأب امرأة وبلغ وظهر علامات الرجال ونحوه حكم بجواز النكاح إلا أنه أذا لم يصل إليها فإنه يؤجل سنة كما يؤجل غيره إذا لم يصل إلى امرأته ولو أن هذا الخنثى المشكل تزوج خنثى مثله فالنكاح يكون موقوفاً إلى أن يستبين حالهما، فإن تبين حالهما فالنكاح جائز ، وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا قبل أن يزول الإشكال لم يتوارثا وإن ماتا وتركا أحد الأبوين فأقام كل واحد من ورثتهما البينة الزوج وأن الأخر هو الزوجة لا يقضى بشيء من ذلك، ولو أن رجلاً قبل هذا الخنثى بشهوة ليس لهذا الرجل أن يتزوج بمحارمه حتى بتبين أمره.
أنه هو قال رحمه الله : (فإن لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع لأن بيت المال أعد لنوائب المسلمين فيدخل في ملكه تعذراً للحاجة وهي حاجة الختان فإذا ختنته تباع ويرد ثمنها إلى بيت المال، فإذا زوج امرأة فختنته ثم طلقها جاز لأنه إن كان ذكراً صح النكاح، وإن كان أنثى فنظر الجنس أخف ثم يفرق بينهما لاحتمال أنه ذكر فيصح النكاح بينهما فتحصل الفرقة ثم تعتد إن خلا بها احتياطاً. ولو حلف بعتق أو طلاق بأن قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت طالق أو فعبدي حر فولدت خنثى لم يقع شيء حتى يستبين لأن الخنثى لم يثبت بالشك، ولو قال كل عبد لي حر أو قال كل أمة لي حرة وله مملوك خنثى لا يعتق حتى يستبين أمرء لما قلنا. وإن قال القولين جميعاً عتق للتيقن بأحد الوصفين لأنه لا يخلو عن أحدهما، وإن قال الخنثى أنا رجل وامرأة لم يقبل قوله إذا كان مشكلاً لأنه دعوى بلا دليل. وذكر في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة : إن قال الخنثى المشكل أنا ذكر أو أنثى كان القول قوله لأن الإنسان أمين في حق نفسه والقول قول الأمين ما لم يعرف خلاف ما قال ما إذا قالت المعتدة انقضت عدتي وأنكر الزوج كان القول قولها ما لم يعرف خلاف قولها بأن قلت في مدة لا تنقضي في مثلها العدة، والأولى ما ذكره في النهاية. ولا يحضر الخنثى غسل رجل ولا امرأة لاحتمال أنه ذكر قبره لأنه أن كان أنثى أقيم ،واجب، وإن كان ذكر لا يضره التسجية. وإذا أراد أن يصلى عليه وعلى رجل وامرأة وضع الرجل مما يلي الأمام والخنثى خلفه والمرأة خلف الخنثى، ويؤخر عن الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويقدم على المرأة لاحتمال أنه رجل. ولو دفن مع رجل في قبر واحد للعذر جعل خلف الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويجعل بينهما حاجزاً . من صعيد ليكون في حكم القبرين وكذا الرجلان إذا دفنا في قبر واحد. وإن دفن مع امرأة قدم الخنثى لاحتمال أنه أنثى، ويدخل قبره ذو رحم محرم منه لاحتمال أنه أنثى. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لما يتعلق بالخنثى من الحدود والقصاص، ولا لما يتعلق به من الأيمان، ولا لما يتعلق به من الدعوى والبينة، ولا لبيان الاختلاف الواقع فيه، ولا لبيان
And the principle regarding marriage matters: If the father marries this hermaphrodite to a woman before his puberty or a wife, then the marriage is suspended, it is not invalid nor void, and they do not inherit from each other until the matter of the hermaphrodite becomes clear, because inheritance is a ruling of an effective marriage, not of a suspended marriage. If the father married him to a woman and he reaches puberty and signs of men appear and the like, then it is judged that the marriage is permissible, except that if he has not consummated, he is given a respite of one year, just as others are given a respite if they do not consummate with their wife. If this ambiguous hermaphrodite marries another hermaphrodite like him, then the marriage is suspended until their situation becomes clear. If their situation becomes clear, the marriage is permissible. If one of them dies or both die before the ambiguity is removed, they do not inherit from each other. If they die and leave one of the parents, and each of their heirs presents proof that the other is the spouse, nothing is judged in that regard. If a man kisses this hermaphrodite with desire, that man may not marry any of his mahrams until the khuntha's matter becomes clear. That is what he said. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has no wealth, then from the public treasury, then she is sold) because the public treasury is prepared for the calamities of Muslims, so she enters into his ownership by necessity for the need, which is the need of circumcision. So when she circumcises him, she is sold and her price is returned to the public treasury. If he marries a woman, and she circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is permissible, because if he is male, the marriage is valid, and if she is female, then the look of one gender to the other is lighter, then they are separated due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage between them is valid, so separation occurs, then she observes the waiting period if he had secluded with her, as a precaution. If he swears an oath of emancipation or divorce, such as saying, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are divorced' or 'my slave is free', and she gives birth to a hermaphrodite, nothing occurs until it becomes clear, because the hermaphrodite is not established by doubt. And if he says, 'Every male slave of mine is free' or says, 'Every female slave of mine is free', and he has a hermaphrodite slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear, for the reason we mentioned. If he says both statements together, he is freed due to certainty of one of the two descriptions, because he is not free of one of them. If the hermaphrodite says, 'I am a man and a woman', his statement is not accepted if he is ambiguous, because it is a claim without evidence. In al-Nihaya, attributed to al-Dhakhira: If the ambiguous hermaphrodite says, 'I am male' or 'I am female', his statement is accepted, because a person is trustworthy regarding his own self, and the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, just as when a woman in her waiting period says her period has ended and the husband denies it, her statement is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, e.g., if she says it within a period that cannot end that way. And the better view is what is mentioned in al-Nihaya. The hermaphrodite should not attend the washing of a man or a woman, due to the possibility that he is male or female. It is recommended to cover his grave because if she is female, it is obligatory to cover her grave, and if he is male, covering does not harm him. When one wants to perform funeral prayer over him together with a man and a woman, the man is placed closest to the imam, the hermaphrodite behind him, and the woman behind the hermaphrodite. He is delayed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and placed ahead of the woman due to the possibility that he is a man. If he is buried with a man in one grave due to an excuse, he is placed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and a barrier of earth is placed between them to be like two graves. Likewise for two men if buried in one grave. If he is buried with a woman, the hermaphrodite is placed in front due to the possibility that he is a man. And a mahram relative may enter his grave due to the possibility that she is female. The author did not address what relates to the hermaphrodite regarding penalties and retribution, nor what relates to oaths, nor what relates to claims and evidence, nor to explain the differences that occur in it, nor to explain...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil), focusing on marriage, oaths, and burial. The author begins with the principle in marriage matters: if the father marries a khuntha to a woman before the khuntha reaches puberty, the marriage is suspended (mawquf). It is neither invalid nor void, and the spouses do not inherit from each other until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because inheritance is a consequence of a valid, effective marriage. If the khuntha later shows male signs, the marriage is judged valid. However, if the husband (the khuntha, now confirmed male) has not consummated, he is given a year to do so, as is the customary period for any husband who has not consummated. If a khuntha marries another khuntha, the marriage is similarly suspended until both become clear. If one dies before clarity, no inheritance occurs. If each side claims the other was the spouse, no judgment is passed. A man who kisses a khuntha with desire may not marry that khuntha's mahrams until the khuntha's gender is known. Regarding circumcision, if the khuntha has no wealth, a slave girl is bought from the public treasury to circumcise him. She is then sold and the price returned. If a woman married the khuntha and she circumcised him, then he divorces her, it is valid: if he is male, the marriage was valid; if she is female (i.e., the khuntha was actually female), the look during circumcision is lighter (since same gender), but then they must separate because the marriage would be invalid, and she must observe the waiting period if there was seclusion, as a precaution. For oaths: if a man swears that if his wife bears a boy she is divorced, and she bears a khuntha, the divorce does not occur until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because the khuntha is not established by doubt. Similarly, if a man says 'all my male slaves are free' and he has a khuntha slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear. But if he says both 'all males are free' and 'all females are free', the khuntha slave is freed because one of the two statements must apply. If a khuntha claims to be both male and female, his word is not accepted. However, if he claims to be male or female specifically, his word is accepted based on the principle that a person is trustworthy regarding themselves, analogous to a woman claiming her waiting period has ended. The author notes that the better view is from al-Nihaya. For burial: the khuntha should not participate in washing a man or a woman due to gender ambiguity. It is recommended to cover the khuntha's grave because if female, covering is obligatory; if male, it does no harm. In funeral prayer with a man and a woman, the man is closest to the imam, then the khuntha, then the woman. He is placed behind the man and ahead of the woman due to possible genders. If buried with a man in one grave, the khuntha is placed behind the man with a dirt barrier. If buried with a woman, the khuntha is placed in front, and a mahram may enter the grave due to possibility of femininity. The author notes that the original matn did not discuss penalties, oaths, claims, etc., for the khuntha.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but whose effects are pending until a condition is fulfilled (e.g., gender clarity).
يستبين (yastabin): Becomes clear or evident; refers to the emergence of definitive gender signs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A khuntha married a woman. Before gender clarity, the khuntha dies. Which statement is correct?
A) The wife inherits because the marriage was valid.
B) The wife inherits half the share.
C) The wife does not inherit because the marriage was suspended.
D) The marriage is void, so no inheritance.

Key Takeaway
A khuntha's marriage is valid but suspended; inheritance is deferred until gender clarity.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
5 min
Marriage Between Two Khuntha and Inheritance Claims
Ruling on marriage of two khuntha and inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling of suspension to marriage between two khuntha and explain why inheritance is denied when both die in ambiguity.

Core Idea
Two khuntha marriage: suspended until both are clear; no inheritance if both die in ambiguity.

When two ambiguous hermaphrodites marry, the same suspension rule applies. This lesson covers the inheritance issue and the evidentiary challenge when heirs claim spousal status.

Guided Path
1
State the suspension rule
The marriage of two khuntha is suspended until both become clear, because the gender of each is unknown.
2
Apply the inheritance rule
If one or both die before clarity, no inheritance passes between them because the marriage never became effective.
3
Examine the evidentiary deadlock
If each set of heirs claims the deceased was the spouse, no judgment is given because there is no basis to prefer one claim.

Source Text

Two khuntha marry. One dies before gender clarity. What is the inheritance ruling?
A) The surviving khuntha inherits half.

Kissing a Khuntha with Desire and Prohibition of Marrying Mahrams
Ruling on kissing a khuntha with desire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a man who kisses a khuntha with desire is prohibited from marrying the khuntha's mahrams until gender clarity.

Core Idea
Kissing a khuntha with desire creates a temporary prohibition on marrying his/her mahrams until gender is known.

Physical contact with a khuntha can create legal consequences. This lesson covers the ruling that a man who kisses a khuntha with desire may not marry the khuntha's mahrams until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, to avoid violating mahram relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is kissing a khuntha with desire (shahwa). This is a form of physical contact that may create a mahram relationship if the khuntha is female.
2
Explain the legal consequence
Because the khuntha could be female, kissing with desire might establish that she is a mahram, so the man cannot marry her mahrams (her father, etc.) until her gender is clear.
3
Note the precautionary nature
This is a precautionary prohibition to prevent possibly marrying a woman who is already a mahram through sexual contact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في مسائل النكاح لو زوج الأب هذا الخنثى امرأة قبل بلوغه أو زوجة فالنكاح موقوف لا يفسد ولا يبطل ولا يتوارثان حتى يستبين أمر الخنثى لأن التوارث حكم النكاح النافذ لا حكم النكاح الموقوف، فإن زوجه الأب امرأة وبلغ وظهر علامات الرجال ونحوه حكم بجواز النكاح إلا أنه أذا لم يصل إليها فإنه يؤجل سنة كما يؤجل غيره إذا لم يصل إلى امرأته ولو أن هذا الخنثى المشكل تزوج خنثى مثله فالنكاح يكون موقوفاً إلى أن يستبين حالهما، فإن تبين حالهما فالنكاح جائز ، وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا قبل أن يزول الإشكال لم يتوارثا وإن ماتا وتركا أحد الأبوين فأقام كل واحد من ورثتهما البينة الزوج وأن الأخر هو الزوجة لا يقضى بشيء من ذلك، ولو أن رجلاً قبل هذا الخنثى بشهوة ليس لهذا الرجل أن يتزوج بمحارمه حتى بتبين أمره.
أنه هو قال رحمه الله : (فإن لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع لأن بيت المال أعد لنوائب المسلمين فيدخل في ملكه تعذراً للحاجة وهي حاجة الختان فإذا ختنته تباع ويرد ثمنها إلى بيت المال، فإذا زوج امرأة فختنته ثم طلقها جاز لأنه إن كان ذكراً صح النكاح، وإن كان أنثى فنظر الجنس أخف ثم يفرق بينهما لاحتمال أنه ذكر فيصح النكاح بينهما فتحصل الفرقة ثم تعتد إن خلا بها احتياطاً. ولو حلف بعتق أو طلاق بأن قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت طالق أو فعبدي حر فولدت خنثى لم يقع شيء حتى يستبين لأن الخنثى لم يثبت بالشك، ولو قال كل عبد لي حر أو قال كل أمة لي حرة وله مملوك خنثى لا يعتق حتى يستبين أمرء لما قلنا. وإن قال القولين جميعاً عتق للتيقن بأحد الوصفين لأنه لا يخلو عن أحدهما، وإن قال الخنثى أنا رجل وامرأة لم يقبل قوله إذا كان مشكلاً لأنه دعوى بلا دليل. وذكر في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة : إن قال الخنثى المشكل أنا ذكر أو أنثى كان القول قوله لأن الإنسان أمين في حق نفسه والقول قول الأمين ما لم يعرف خلاف ما قال ما إذا قالت المعتدة انقضت عدتي وأنكر الزوج كان القول قولها ما لم يعرف خلاف قولها بأن قلت في مدة لا تنقضي في مثلها العدة، والأولى ما ذكره في النهاية. ولا يحضر الخنثى غسل رجل ولا امرأة لاحتمال أنه ذكر قبره لأنه أن كان أنثى أقيم ،واجب، وإن كان ذكر لا يضره التسجية. وإذا أراد أن يصلى عليه وعلى رجل وامرأة وضع الرجل مما يلي الأمام والخنثى خلفه والمرأة خلف الخنثى، ويؤخر عن الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويقدم على المرأة لاحتمال أنه رجل. ولو دفن مع رجل في قبر واحد للعذر جعل خلف الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويجعل بينهما حاجزاً . من صعيد ليكون في حكم القبرين وكذا الرجلان إذا دفنا في قبر واحد. وإن دفن مع امرأة قدم الخنثى لاحتمال أنه أنثى، ويدخل قبره ذو رحم محرم منه لاحتمال أنه أنثى. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لما يتعلق بالخنثى من الحدود والقصاص، ولا لما يتعلق به من الأيمان، ولا لما يتعلق به من الدعوى والبينة، ولا لبيان الاختلاف الواقع فيه، ولا لبيان
And the principle regarding marriage matters: If the father marries this hermaphrodite to a woman before his puberty or a wife, then the marriage is suspended, it is not invalid nor void, and they do not inherit from each other until the matter of the hermaphrodite becomes clear, because inheritance is a ruling of an effective marriage, not of a suspended marriage. If the father married him to a woman and he reaches puberty and signs of men appear and the like, then it is judged that the marriage is permissible, except that if he has not consummated, he is given a respite of one year, just as others are given a respite if they do not consummate with their wife. If this ambiguous hermaphrodite marries another hermaphrodite like him, then the marriage is suspended until their situation becomes clear. If their situation becomes clear, the marriage is permissible. If one of them dies or both die before the ambiguity is removed, they do not inherit from each other. If they die and leave one of the parents, and each of their heirs presents proof that the other is the spouse, nothing is judged in that regard. If a man kisses this hermaphrodite with desire, that man may not marry any of his mahrams until the khuntha's matter becomes clear. That is what he said. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has no wealth, then from the public treasury, then she is sold) because the public treasury is prepared for the calamities of Muslims, so she enters into his ownership by necessity for the need, which is the need of circumcision. So when she circumcises him, she is sold and her price is returned to the public treasury. If he marries a woman, and she circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is permissible, because if he is male, the marriage is valid, and if she is female, then the look of one gender to the other is lighter, then they are separated due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage between them is valid, so separation occurs, then she observes the waiting period if he had secluded with her, as a precaution. If he swears an oath of emancipation or divorce, such as saying, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are divorced' or 'my slave is free', and she gives birth to a hermaphrodite, nothing occurs until it becomes clear, because the hermaphrodite is not established by doubt. And if he says, 'Every male slave of mine is free' or says, 'Every female slave of mine is free', and he has a hermaphrodite slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear, for the reason we mentioned. If he says both statements together, he is freed due to certainty of one of the two descriptions, because he is not free of one of them. If the hermaphrodite says, 'I am a man and a woman', his statement is not accepted if he is ambiguous, because it is a claim without evidence. In al-Nihaya, attributed to al-Dhakhira: If the ambiguous hermaphrodite says, 'I am male' or 'I am female', his statement is accepted, because a person is trustworthy regarding his own self, and the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, just as when a woman in her waiting period says her period has ended and the husband denies it, her statement is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, e.g., if she says it within a period that cannot end that way. And the better view is what is mentioned in al-Nihaya. The hermaphrodite should not attend the washing of a man or a woman, due to the possibility that he is male or female. It is recommended to cover his grave because if she is female, it is obligatory to cover her grave, and if he is male, covering does not harm him. When one wants to perform funeral prayer over him together with a man and a woman, the man is placed closest to the imam, the hermaphrodite behind him, and the woman behind the hermaphrodite. He is delayed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and placed ahead of the woman due to the possibility that he is a man. If he is buried with a man in one grave due to an excuse, he is placed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and a barrier of earth is placed between them to be like two graves. Likewise for two men if buried in one grave. If he is buried with a woman, the hermaphrodite is placed in front due to the possibility that he is a man. And a mahram relative may enter his grave due to the possibility that she is female. The author did not address what relates to the hermaphrodite regarding penalties and retribution, nor what relates to oaths, nor what relates to claims and evidence, nor to explain the differences that occur in it, nor to explain...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil), focusing on marriage, oaths, and burial. The author begins with the principle in marriage matters: if the father marries a khuntha to a woman before the khuntha reaches puberty, the marriage is suspended (mawquf). It is neither invalid nor void, and the spouses do not inherit from each other until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because inheritance is a consequence of a valid, effective marriage. If the khuntha later shows male signs, the marriage is judged valid. However, if the husband (the khuntha, now confirmed male) has not consummated, he is given a year to do so, as is the customary period for any husband who has not consummated. If a khuntha marries another khuntha, the marriage is similarly suspended until both become clear. If one dies before clarity, no inheritance occurs. If each side claims the other was the spouse, no judgment is passed. A man who kisses a khuntha with desire may not marry that khuntha's mahrams until the khuntha's gender is known. Regarding circumcision, if the khuntha has no wealth, a slave girl is bought from the public treasury to circumcise him. She is then sold and the price returned. If a woman married the khuntha and she circumcised him, then he divorces her, it is valid: if he is male, the marriage was valid; if she is female (i.e., the khuntha was actually female), the look during circumcision is lighter (since same gender), but then they must separate because the marriage would be invalid, and she must observe the waiting period if there was seclusion, as a precaution. For oaths: if a man swears that if his wife bears a boy she is divorced, and she bears a khuntha, the divorce does not occur until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because the khuntha is not established by doubt. Similarly, if a man says 'all my male slaves are free' and he has a khuntha slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear. But if he says both 'all males are free' and 'all females are free', the khuntha slave is freed because one of the two statements must apply. If a khuntha claims to be both male and female, his word is not accepted. However, if he claims to be male or female specifically, his word is accepted based on the principle that a person is trustworthy regarding themselves, analogous to a woman claiming her waiting period has ended. The author notes that the better view is from al-Nihaya. For burial: the khuntha should not participate in washing a man or a woman due to gender ambiguity. It is recommended to cover the khuntha's grave because if female, covering is obligatory; if male, it does no harm. In funeral prayer with a man and a woman, the man is closest to the imam, then the khuntha, then the woman. He is placed behind the man and ahead of the woman due to possible genders. If buried with a man in one grave, the khuntha is placed behind the man with a dirt barrier. If buried with a woman, the khuntha is placed in front, and a mahram may enter the grave due to possibility of femininity. The author notes that the original matn did not discuss penalties, oaths, claims, etc., for the khuntha.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but whose effects are pending until a condition is fulfilled (e.g., gender clarity).
يستبين (yastabin): Becomes clear or evident; refers to the emergence of definitive gender signs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man kisses a khuntha with desire. The khuntha's gender later becomes clear as male. Can the man now marry the khuntha's sister?
A) Yes, because the khuntha is male, so no mahram relationship.
B) No, because the kiss created a permanent prohibition.
C) Yes, but only if the sister consents.
D) No, because the khuntha's mahrams are always forbidden.

Key Takeaway
Kissing a khuntha with desire temporarily prohibits marrying his/her mahrams until gender clarity.

Circumcision of a Khuntha Using Public Treasury
Ruling on circumcision financing for a khuntha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on circumcising a khuntha using public funds and the subsequent sale of the slave girl.

Core Idea
A khuntha's circumcision is necessary; if he has no wealth, a slave girl is bought from the public treasury, used, and then sold.

Circumcision is required for both males and females in Islam, but for a khuntha, the act must be done without violating modesty. This lesson explains the financial and legal mechanism to ensure circumcision while preserving the slave girl's rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the need
Circumcision is necessary. The khuntha may not have the means to pay for it.
2
Describe the solution
A slave girl is purchased from the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal) to perform the circumcision. She is then sold, and the money is returned to the treasury.
3
Explain the divorce scenario
If the khuntha married a woman and she circumcised him, then he divorces her, the divorce is valid. If the khuntha is male, the marriage was valid; if female, the circumcision involved looking at the same gender (lighter) but the marriage is invalid and separation occurs with iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في مسائل النكاح لو زوج الأب هذا الخنثى امرأة قبل بلوغه أو زوجة فالنكاح موقوف لا يفسد ولا يبطل ولا يتوارثان حتى يستبين أمر الخنثى لأن التوارث حكم النكاح النافذ لا حكم النكاح الموقوف، فإن زوجه الأب امرأة وبلغ وظهر علامات الرجال ونحوه حكم بجواز النكاح إلا أنه أذا لم يصل إليها فإنه يؤجل سنة كما يؤجل غيره إذا لم يصل إلى امرأته ولو أن هذا الخنثى المشكل تزوج خنثى مثله فالنكاح يكون موقوفاً إلى أن يستبين حالهما، فإن تبين حالهما فالنكاح جائز ، وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا قبل أن يزول الإشكال لم يتوارثا وإن ماتا وتركا أحد الأبوين فأقام كل واحد من ورثتهما البينة الزوج وأن الأخر هو الزوجة لا يقضى بشيء من ذلك، ولو أن رجلاً قبل هذا الخنثى بشهوة ليس لهذا الرجل أن يتزوج بمحارمه حتى بتبين أمره.

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil), focusing on marriage, oaths, and burial. The author begins with the principle in marriage matters: if the father marries a khuntha to a woman before the khuntha reaches puberty, the marriage is suspended (mawquf). It is neither invalid nor void, and the spouses do not inherit from each other until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because inheritance is a consequence of a valid, effective marriage. If the khuntha later shows male signs, the marriage is judged valid. However, if the husband (the khuntha, now confirmed male) has not consummated, he is given a year to do so, as is the customary period for any husband who has not consummated. If a khuntha marries another khuntha, the marriage is similarly suspended until both become clear. If one dies before clarity, no inheritance occurs. If each side claims the other was the spouse, no judgment is passed. A man who kisses a khuntha with desire may not marry that khuntha's mahrams until the khuntha's gender is known. Regarding circumcision, if the khuntha has no wealth, a slave girl is bought from the public treasury to circumcise him. She is then sold and the price returned. For oaths: if a man swears that if his wife bears a boy she is divorced, and she bears a khuntha, the divorce does not occur until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because the khuntha is not established by doubt. Similarly, if a man says 'all my male slaves are free' and he has a khuntha slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear. But if he says both 'all males are free' and 'all females are free', the khuntha slave is freed because one of the two statements must apply. If a khuntha claims to be both male and female, his word is not accepted. However, if he claims to be male or female specifically, his word is accepted based on the principle that a person is trustworthy regarding themselves, analogous to a woman claiming her waiting period has ended. The author notes that the better view is from al-Nihaya. For burial: the khuntha should not participate in washing a man or a woman due to gender ambiguity. It is recommended to cover the khuntha's grave because if female, covering is obligatory; if male, it does no harm. In funeral prayer with a man and a woman, the man is closest to the imam, then the khuntha, then the woman. He is placed behind the man and ahead of the woman due to possible genders. If buried with a man in one grave, the khuntha is placed behind the man with a dirt barrier. If buried with a woman, the khuntha is placed in front, and a mahram may enter the grave due to possibility of femininity. The author notes that the original matn did not discuss penalties, oaths, claims, etc., for the khuntha.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but whose effects are pending until a condition is fulfilled (e.g., gender clarity).
يستبين (yastabin): Becomes clear or evident; refers to the emergence of definitive gender signs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a slave girl circumcises a khuntha, what happens to her?
A) She becomes the khuntha's permanent slave.
B) She is set free.
C) She is sold and the money goes to the treasury.
D) She is returned to the original owner.

Key Takeaway
The public treasury funds necessary circumcision for a khuntha via a temporary slave purchase.
