Oaths of Divorce and Emancipation Regarding a Khuntha
Ruling on oaths concerning a khuntha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling that an oath involving a khuntha does not take effect until gender clarity in some cases, and explain the exception for comprehensive statements.

Core Idea
Oaths about a khuntha child or slave are suspended until gender clarity unless the oath covers both possibilities.

When a person makes an oath of divorce or emancipation conditioned on gender, and the result is a khuntha, the effect is suspended because the condition's fulfillment is uncertain. However, if the oath encompasses both genders, the effect occurs immediately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath type
The oath is conditional: 'if the child is a boy, divorce' or 'all male slaves are free.'
2
Apply the suspension rule
Since the khuntha is neither clearly male nor female, the condition is not met. The oath does not take effect until gender clarity.
3
Consider the comprehensive oath
If the master says both 'all male slaves are free' and 'all female slaves are free', the khuntha slave is freed immediately because one of the statements must apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في مسائل النكاح لو زوج الأب هذا الخنثى امرأة قبل بلوغه أو زوجة فالنكاح موقوف لا يفسد ولا يبطل ولا يتوارثان حتى يستبين أمر الخنثى لأن التوارث حكم النكاح النافذ لا حكم النكاح الموقوف، فإن زوجه الأب امرأة وبلغ وظهر علامات الرجال ونحوه حكم بجواز النكاح إلا أنه أذا لم يصل إليها فإنه يؤجل سنة كما يؤجل غيره إذا لم يصل إلى امرأته ولو أن هذا الخنثى المشكل تزوج خنثى مثله فالنكاح يكون موقوفاً إلى أن يستبين حالهما، فإن تبين حالهما فالنكاح جائز ، وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا قبل أن يزول الإشكال لم يتوارثا وإن ماتا وتركا أحد الأبوين فأقام كل واحد من ورثتهما البينة الزوج وأن الأخر هو الزوجة لا يقضى بشيء من ذلك، ولو أن رجلاً قبل هذا الخنثى بشهوة ليس لهذا الرجل أن يتزوج بمحارمه حتى بتبين أمره.
أنه هو قال رحمه الله : (فإن لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع لأن بيت المال أعد لنوائب المسلمين فيدخل في ملكه تعذراً للحاجة وهي حاجة الختان فإذا ختنته تباع ويرد ثمنها إلى بيت المال، فإذا زوج امرأة فختنته ثم طلقها جاز لأنه إن كان ذكراً صح النكاح، وإن كان أنثى فنظر الجنس أخف ثم يفرق بينهما لاحتمال أنه ذكر فيصح النكاح بينهما فتحصل الفرقة ثم تعتد إن خلا بها احتياطاً. ولو حلف بعتق أو طلاق بأن قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت طالق أو فعبدي حر فولدت خنثى لم يقع شيء حتى يستبين لأن الخنثى لم يثبت بالشك، ولو قال كل عبد لي حر أو قال كل أمة لي حرة وله مملوك خنثى لا يعتق حتى يستبين أمرء لما قلنا. وإن قال القولين جميعاً عتق للتيقن بأحد الوصفين لأنه لا يخلو عن أحدهما، وإن قال الخنثى أنا رجل وامرأة لم يقبل قوله إذا كان مشكلاً لأنه دعوى بلا دليل. وذكر في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة : إن قال الخنثى المشكل أنا ذكر أو أنثى كان القول قوله لأن الإنسان أمين في حق نفسه والقول قول الأمين ما لم يعرف خلاف ما قال ما إذا قالت المعتدة انقضت عدتي وأنكر الزوج كان القول قولها ما لم يعرف خلاف قولها بأن قلت في مدة لا تنقضي في مثلها العدة، والأولى ما ذكره في النهاية. ولا يحضر الخنثى غسل رجل ولا امرأة لاحتمال أنه ذكر قبره لأنه أن كان أنثى أقيم ،واجب، وإن كان ذكر لا يضره التسجية. وإذا أراد أن يصلى عليه وعلى رجل وامرأة وضع الرجل مما يلي الأمام والخنثى خلفه والمرأة خلف الخنثى، ويؤخر عن الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويقدم على المرأة لاحتمال أنه رجل. ولو دفن مع رجل في قبر واحد للعذر جعل خلف الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويجعل بينهما حاجزاً . من صعيد ليكون في حكم القبرين وكذا الرجلان إذا دفنا في قبر واحد. وإن دفن مع امرأة قدم الخنثى لاحتمال أنه أنثى، ويدخل قبره ذو رحم محرم منه لاحتمال أنه أنثى. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لما يتعلق بالخنثى من الحدود والقصاص، ولا لما يتعلق به من الأيمان، ولا لما يتعلق به من الدعوى والبينة، ولا لبيان الاختلاف الواقع فيه، ولا لبيان
And the principle regarding marriage matters: If the father marries this hermaphrodite to a woman before his puberty or a wife, then the marriage is suspended, it is not invalid nor void, and they do not inherit from each other until the matter of the hermaphrodite becomes clear, because inheritance is a ruling of an effective marriage, not of a suspended marriage. If the father married him to a woman and he reaches puberty and signs of men appear and the like, then it is judged that the marriage is permissible, except that if he has not consummated, he is given a respite of one year, just as others are given a respite if they do not consummate with their wife. If this ambiguous hermaphrodite marries another hermaphrodite like him, then the marriage is suspended until their situation becomes clear. If their situation becomes clear, the marriage is permissible. If one of them dies or both die before the ambiguity is removed, they do not inherit from each other. If they die and leave one of the parents, and each of their heirs presents proof that the other is the spouse, nothing is judged in that regard. If a man kisses this hermaphrodite with desire, that man may not marry any of his mahrams until the khuntha's matter becomes clear. That is what he said. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has no wealth, then from the public treasury, then she is sold) because the public treasury is prepared for the calamities of Muslims, so she enters into his ownership by necessity for the need, which is the need of circumcision. So when she circumcises him, she is sold and her price is returned to the public treasury. If he marries a woman, and she circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is permissible, because if he is male, the marriage is valid, and if she is female, then the look of one gender to the other is lighter, then they are separated due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage between them is valid, so separation occurs, then she observes the waiting period if he had secluded with her, as a precaution. If he swears an oath of emancipation or divorce, such as saying, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are divorced' or 'my slave is free', and she gives birth to a hermaphrodite, nothing occurs until it becomes clear, because the hermaphrodite is not established by doubt. And if he says, 'Every male slave of mine is free' or says, 'Every female slave of mine is free', and he has a hermaphrodite slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear, for the reason we mentioned. If he says both statements together, he is freed due to certainty of one of the two descriptions, because he is not free of one of them. If the hermaphrodite says, 'I am a man and a woman', his statement is not accepted if he is ambiguous, because it is a claim without evidence. In al-Nihaya, attributed to al-Dhakhira: If the ambiguous hermaphrodite says, 'I am male' or 'I am female', his statement is accepted, because a person is trustworthy regarding his own self, and the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, just as when a woman in her waiting period says her period has ended and the husband denies it, her statement is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, e.g., if she says it within a period that cannot end that way. And the better view is what is mentioned in al-Nihaya. The hermaphrodite should not attend the washing of a man or a woman, due to the possibility that he is male or female. It is recommended to cover his grave because if she is female, it is obligatory to cover her grave, and if he is male, covering does not harm him. When one wants to perform funeral prayer over him together with a man and a woman, the man is placed closest to the imam, the hermaphrodite behind him, and the woman behind the hermaphrodite. He is delayed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and placed ahead of the woman due to the possibility that he is a man. If he is buried with a man in one grave due to an excuse, he is placed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and a barrier of earth is placed between them to be like two graves. Likewise for two men if buried in one grave. If he is buried with a woman, the hermaphrodite is placed in front due to the possibility that he is a man. And a mahram relative may enter his grave due to the possibility that she is female. The author did not address what relates to the hermaphrodite regarding penalties and retribution, nor what relates to oaths, nor what relates to claims and evidence, nor to explain the differences that occur in it, nor to explain...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil), focusing on marriage, oaths, and burial. The author begins with the principle in marriage matters: if the father marries a khuntha to a woman before the khuntha reaches puberty, the marriage is suspended (mawquf). It is neither invalid nor void, and the spouses do not inherit from each other until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because inheritance is a consequence of a valid, effective marriage. If the khuntha later shows male signs, the marriage is judged valid. However, if the husband (the khuntha, now confirmed male) has not consummated, he is given a year to do so, as is the customary period for any husband who has not consummated. If a khuntha marries another khuntha, the marriage is similarly suspended until both become clear. If one dies before clarity, no inheritance occurs. If each side claims the other was the spouse, no judgment is passed. A man who kisses a khuntha with desire may not marry that khuntha's mahrams until the khuntha's gender is known. Regarding circumcision, if the khuntha has no wealth, a slave girl is bought from the public treasury to circumcise him. She is then sold and the price returned. If a woman married the khuntha and she circumcised him, then he divorces her, it is valid: if he is male, the marriage was valid; if she is female (i.e., the khuntha was actually female), the look during circumcision is lighter (since same gender), but then they must separate because the marriage would be invalid, and she must observe the waiting period if there was seclusion, as a precaution. For oaths: if a man swears that if his wife bears a boy she is divorced, and she bears a khuntha, the divorce does not occur until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because the khuntha is not established by doubt. Similarly, if a man says 'all my male slaves are free' and he has a khuntha slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear. But if he says both 'all males are free' and 'all females are free', the khuntha slave is freed because one of the two statements must apply. If a khuntha claims to be both male and female, his word is not accepted. However, if he claims to be male or female specifically, his word is accepted based on the principle that a person is trustworthy regarding themselves, analogous to a woman claiming her waiting period has ended. The author notes that the better view is from al-Nihaya. For burial: the khuntha should not participate in washing a man or a woman due to gender ambiguity. It is recommended to cover the khuntha's grave because if female, covering is obligatory; if male, it does no harm. In funeral prayer with a man and a woman, the man is closest to the imam, then the khuntha, then the woman. He is placed behind the man and ahead of the woman due to possible genders. If buried with a man in one grave, the khuntha is placed behind the man with a dirt barrier. If buried with a woman, the khuntha is placed in front, and a mahram may enter the grave due to possibility of femininity. The author notes that the original matn did not discuss penalties, oaths, claims, etc., for the khuntha.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but whose effects are pending until a condition is fulfilled (e.g., gender clarity).
يستبين (yastabin): Becomes clear or evident; refers to the emergence of definitive gender signs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says: 'Every male slave I have is free.' He has a khuntha slave. Is the slave freed?
A) Yes, because the slave is potentially male.
B) No, because his gender is uncertain.
C) Yes, but only after a year.
D) No, because the slave is considered female.

Key Takeaway
Oaths conditioned on gender are suspended for a khuntha unless both genders are encompassed.

Claim of Gender by a Khuntha
Ruling on a khuntha's claim about their gender.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between accepted and rejected claims of gender by a khuntha based on the principle of trustworthiness.

Core Idea
A khuntha's claim to be both genders is rejected; a claim to be one specific gender is accepted due to self-trustworthiness.

When a khuntha makes a statement about his/her own gender, the law must decide its validity. This lesson explains that a claim of being both male and female is rejected as baseless, but a claim of being one or the other is accepted, analogous to a woman's claim about her waiting period.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two claims
If the khuntha says 'I am both male and female', it is a claim without evidence and rejected. If he says 'I am male' or 'I am female', it is accepted because a person is trusted about themselves.
2
Identify the legal principle
The principle: 'al-insan amin fi haqq nafsih' (a person is trustworthy regarding their own self).
3
Apply the analogy
This is analogous to a woman claiming her waiting period has ended; her word is accepted unless contradicted by evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If each side claims the other was the spouse, no judgment is passed. A man who kisses a khuntha with desire may not marry that khuntha's mahrams until the khuntha's gender is known. Regarding circumcision, if the khuntha has no wealth, a slave girl is bought from the public treasury to circumcise him. She is then sold and the price returned. If a woman married the khuntha and she circumcised him, then he divorces her, it is valid: if he is male, the marriage was valid; if she is female (i.e., the khuntha was actually female), the look during circumcision is lighter (since same gender), but then they must separate because the marriage would be invalid, and she must observe the waiting period if there was seclusion, as a precaution. For oaths: if a man swears that if his wife bears a boy she is divorced, and she bears a khuntha, the divorce does not occur until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because the khuntha is not established by doubt. Similarly, if a man says 'all my male slaves are free' and he has a khuntha slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear. But if he says both 'all males are free' and 'all females are free', the khuntha slave is freed because one of the two statements must apply. If a khuntha claims to be both male and female, his word is not accepted. However, if he claims to be male or female specifically, his word is accepted based on the principle that a person is trustworthy regarding themselves, analogous to a woman claiming her waiting period has ended. The author notes that the better view is from al-Nihaya. For burial: the khuntha should not participate in washing a man or a woman due to gender ambiguity. It is recommended to cover the khuntha's grave because if female, covering is obligatory; if male, it does no harm. In funeral prayer with a man and a woman, the man is closest to the imam, then the khuntha, then the woman. He is placed behind the man and ahead of the woman due to possible genders. If buried with a man in one grave, the khuntha is placed behind the man with a dirt barrier. If buried with a woman, the khuntha is placed in front, and a mahram may enter the grave due to possibility of femininity. The author notes that the original matn did not discuss penalties, oaths, claims, etc., for the khuntha.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but whose effects are pending until a condition is fulfilled (e.g., gender clarity).
يستبين (yastabin): Becomes clear or evident; refers to the emergence of definitive gender signs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A khuntha says: 'I am a man.' Based on the passage, what is the ruling?
A) The statement is rejected because he is ambiguous.
B) The statement is accepted because he is trustworthy about himself.
C) The statement is accepted only if a doctor agrees.
D) The statement is rejected because it might be false.

Key Takeaway
A khuntha's claim of a single gender is accepted unless contrary evidence arises.

Burial and Funeral Arrangements for a Khuntha
Rulings on burial of a khuntha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings for washing, burial, and funeral prayer for a khuntha in relation to men and women.

Core Idea
A khuntha is treated with maximum caution in burial: placed behind the man and ahead of the woman, with a barrier when buried with the same sex.

Due to gender ambiguity, the funeral arrangements for a khuntha require careful positioning to respect both possibilities. This lesson covers the rules for washing, covering the grave, and placement in prayer and burial relative to men and women, as well as who may enter the grave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition
The khuntha may not wash a man or a woman because his/her gender is unknown; it could be the opposite gender.
2
Position in funeral prayer
When praying with a man and a woman, the man is closest to the imam, then the khuntha, then the woman. The khuntha is behind the man (in case she is female) and ahead of the woman (in case he is male).
3
Position in burial
If buried with a man, the khuntha is placed behind the man with a barrier of earth. If buried with a woman, the khuntha is placed in front. A mahram may enter the grave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في مسائل النكاح لو زوج الأب هذا الخنثى امرأة قبل بلوغه أو زوجة فالنكاح موقوف لا يفسد ولا يبطل ولا يتوارثان حتى يستبين أمر الخنثى لأن التوارث حكم النكاح النافذ لا حكم النكاح الموقوف، فإن زوجه الأب امرأة وبلغ وظهر علامات الرجال ونحوه حكم بجواز النكاح إلا أنه أذا لم يصل إليها فإنه يؤجل سنة كما يؤجل غيره إذا لم يصل إلى امرأته ولو أن هذا الخنثى المشكل تزوج خنثى مثله فالنكاح يكون موقوفاً إلى أن يستبين حالهما، فإن تبين حالهما فالنكاح جائز ، وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا قبل أن يزول الإشكال لم يتوارثا وإن ماتا وتركا أحد الأبوين فأقام كل واحد من ورثتهما البينة الزوج وأن الأخر هو الزوجة لا يقضى بشيء من ذلك، ولو أن رجلاً قبل هذا الخنثى بشهوة ليس لهذا الرجل أن يتزوج بمحارمه حتى بتبين أمره.
أنه هو قال رحمه الله : (فإن لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع لأن بيت المال أعد لنوائب المسلمين فيدخل في ملكه تعذراً للحاجة وهي حاجة الختان فإذا ختنته تباع ويرد ثمنها إلى بيت المال، فإذا زوج امرأة فختنته ثم طلقها جاز لأنه إن كان ذكراً صح النكاح، وإن كان أنثى فنظر الجنس أخف ثم يفرق بينهما لاحتمال أنه ذكر فيصح النكاح بينهما فتحصل الفرقة ثم تعتد إن خلا بها احتياطاً. ولو حلف بعتق أو طلاق بأن قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت طالق أو فعبدي حر فولدت خنثى لم يقع شيء حتى يستبين لأن الخنثى لم يثبت بالشك، ولو قال كل عبد لي حر أو قال كل أمة لي حرة وله مملوك خنثى لا يعتق حتى يستبين أمرء لما قلنا. وإن قال القولين جميعاً عتق للتيقن بأحد الوصفين لأنه لا يخلو عن أحدهما، وإن قال الخنثى أنا رجل وامرأة لم يقبل قوله إذا كان مشكلاً لأنه دعوى بلا دليل. وذكر في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة : إن قال الخنثى المشكل أنا ذكر أو أنثى كان القول قوله لأن الإنسان أمين في حق نفسه والقول قول الأمين ما لم يعرف خلاف ما قال ما إذا قالت المعتدة انقضت عدتي وأنكر الزوج كان القول قولها ما لم يعرف خلاف قولها بأن قلت في مدة لا تنقضي في مثلها العدة، والأولى ما ذكره في النهاية. ولا يحضر الخنثى غسل رجل ولا امرأة لاحتمال أنه ذكر قبره لأنه أن كان أنثى أقيم ،واجب، وإن كان ذكر لا يضره التسجية. وإذا أراد أن يصلى عليه وعلى رجل وامرأة وضع الرجل مما يلي الأمام والخنثى خلفه والمرأة خلف الخنثى، ويؤخر عن الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويقدم على المرأة لاحتمال أنه رجل. ولو دفن مع رجل في قبر واحد للعذر جعل خلف الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويجعل بينهما حاجزاً . من صعيد ليكون في حكم القبرين وكذا الرجلان إذا دفنا في قبر واحد. وإن دفن مع امرأة قدم الخنثى لاحتمال أنه أنثى، ويدخل قبره ذو رحم محرم منه لاحتمال أنه أنثى. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لما يتعلق بالخنثى من الحدود والقصاص، ولا لما يتعلق به من الأيمان، ولا لما يتعلق به من الدعوى والبينة، ولا لبيان الاختلاف الواقع فيه، ولا لبيان
And the principle regarding marriage matters: If the father marries this hermaphrodite to a woman before his puberty or a wife, then the marriage is suspended, it is not invalid nor void, and they do not inherit from each other until the matter of the hermaphrodite becomes clear, because inheritance is a ruling of an effective marriage, not of a suspended marriage. If the father married him to a woman and he reaches puberty and signs of men appear and the like, then it is judged that the marriage is permissible, except that if he has not consummated, he is given a respite of one year, just as others are given a respite if they do not consummate with their wife. If this ambiguous hermaphrodite marries another hermaphrodite like him, then the marriage is suspended until their situation becomes clear. If their situation becomes clear, the marriage is permissible. If one of them dies or both die before the ambiguity is removed, they do not inherit from each other. If they die and leave one of the parents, and each of their heirs presents proof that the other is the spouse, nothing is judged in that regard. If a man kisses this hermaphrodite with desire, that man may not marry any of his mahrams until the khuntha's matter becomes clear. That is what he said. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has no wealth, then from the public treasury, then she is sold) because the public treasury is prepared for the calamities of Muslims, so she enters into his ownership by necessity for the need, which is the need of circumcision. So when she circumcises him, she is sold and her price is returned to the public treasury. If he marries a woman, and she circumcises him, then he divorces her, it is permissible, because if he is male, the marriage is valid, and if she is female, then the look of one gender to the other is lighter, then they are separated due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage between them is valid, so separation occurs, then she observes the waiting period if he had secluded with her, as a precaution. If he swears an oath of emancipation or divorce, such as saying, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are divorced' or 'my slave is free', and she gives birth to a hermaphrodite, nothing occurs until it becomes clear, because the hermaphrodite is not established by doubt. And if he says, 'Every male slave of mine is free' or says, 'Every female slave of mine is free', and he has a hermaphrodite slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear, for the reason we mentioned. If he says both statements together, he is freed due to certainty of one of the two descriptions, because he is not free of one of them. If the hermaphrodite says, 'I am a man and a woman', his statement is not accepted if he is ambiguous, because it is a claim without evidence. In al-Nihaya, attributed to al-Dhakhira: If the ambiguous hermaphrodite says, 'I am male' or 'I am female', his statement is accepted, because a person is trustworthy regarding his own self, and the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, just as when a woman in her waiting period says her period has ended and the husband denies it, her statement is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, e.g., if she says it within a period that cannot end that way. And the better view is what is mentioned in al-Nihaya. The hermaphrodite should not attend the washing of a man or a woman, due to the possibility that he is male or female. It is recommended to cover his grave because if she is female, it is obligatory to cover her grave, and if he is male, covering does not harm him. When one wants to perform funeral prayer over him together with a man and a woman, the man is placed closest to the imam, the hermaphrodite behind him, and the woman behind the hermaphrodite. He is delayed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and placed ahead of the woman due to the possibility that he is a man. If he is buried with a man in one grave due to an excuse, he is placed behind the man due to the possibility that she is a woman, and a barrier of earth is placed between them to be like two graves. Likewise for two men if buried in one grave. If he is buried with a woman, the hermaphrodite is placed in front due to the possibility that he is a man. And a mahram relative may enter his grave due to the possibility that she is female. The author did not address what relates to the hermaphrodite regarding penalties and retribution, nor what relates to oaths, nor what relates to claims and evidence, nor to explain the differences that occur in it, nor to explain...

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil), focusing on marriage, oaths, and burial. The author begins with the principle in marriage matters: if the father marries a khuntha to a woman before the khuntha reaches puberty, the marriage is suspended (mawquf). It is neither invalid nor void, and the spouses do not inherit from each other until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because inheritance is a consequence of a valid, effective marriage. If the khuntha later shows male signs, the marriage is judged valid. However, if the husband (the khuntha, now confirmed male) has not consummated, he is given a year to do so, as is the customary period for any husband who has not consummated. If a khuntha marries another khuntha, the marriage is similarly suspended until both become clear. If one dies before clarity, no inheritance occurs. If each side claims the other was the spouse, no judgment is passed. A man who kisses a khuntha with desire may not marry that khuntha's mahrams until the khuntha's gender is known. Regarding circumcision, if the khuntha has no wealth, a slave girl is bought from the public treasury to circumcise him. She is then sold and the price returned. If a woman married the khuntha and she circumcised him, then he divorces her, it is valid: if he is male, the marriage was valid; if she is female (i.e., the khuntha was actually female), the look during circumcision is lighter (since same gender), but then they must separate because the marriage would be invalid, and she must observe the waiting period if there was seclusion, as a precaution. For oaths: if a man swears that if his wife bears a boy she is divorced, and she bears a khuntha, the divorce does not occur until the khuntha's gender becomes clear, because the khuntha is not established by doubt. Similarly, if a man says 'all my male slaves are free' and he has a khuntha slave, he is not freed until his matter becomes clear. But if he says both 'all males are free' and 'all females are free', the khuntha slave is freed because one of the two statements must apply. If a khuntha claims to be both male and female, his word is not accepted. However, if he claims to be male or female specifically, his word is accepted based on the principle that a person is trustworthy regarding themselves, analogous to a woman claiming her waiting period has ended. The author notes that the better view is from al-Nihaya. For burial: the khuntha should not participate in washing a man or a woman due to gender ambiguity. It is recommended to cover the khuntha's grave because if female, covering is obligatory; if male, it does no harm. In funeral prayer with a man and a woman, the man is closest to the imam, then the khuntha, then the woman. He is placed behind the man and ahead of the woman due to possible genders. If buried with a man in one grave, the khuntha is placed behind the man with a dirt barrier. If buried with a woman, the khuntha is placed in front, and a mahram may enter the grave due to possibility of femininity. The author notes that the original matn did not discuss penalties, oaths, claims, etc., for the khuntha.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but whose effects are pending until a condition is fulfilled (e.g., gender clarity).
يستبين (yastabin): Becomes clear or evident; refers to the emergence of definitive gender signs.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Suspended Marriage of the Khuntha Mushkil
Rulings on marriage and inheritance of khuntha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on nikah mawquf for a khuntha mushkil and identify when inheritance applies.

Core Idea
A khuntha's marriage is suspended—valid but no inheritance until gender is clear.

The khuntha mushkil presents a challenge in marriage law because gender determines legal effects. The Hanafi school introduces the concept of nikah mawquf (suspended marriage): the contract is valid but its full effects, especially inheritance, are delayed until the khuntha's gender becomes known. This lesson covers the rules for marriage of a khuntha with a non-khuntha, with another khuntha, and the consequences of death before clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the marital scenarios
The source covers three cases: khuntha married by father to a woman, khuntha married to another khuntha, and a man who kisses a khuntha. Understand each scenario and the ruling (valid, suspended, or prohibition to marry maharim).
2
Analyze the concept of nikah mawquf
The text explains that marriage of a khuntha is 'mawquf' (suspended) until the gender is known. This means the contract is not fasid or batil but its inheritance effects are withheld. Why? Because inheritance is a ruling of a nafidh (effective) marriage.
Compare with normal marriage: a valid marriage immediately creates inheritance rights.
3
Apply the ruling to inheritance
If a khuntha dies before clarity, there is no inheritance between spouses. Work through the example: two khuntha marry, one dies, no inheritance. If both die leaving one parent, and each heir claims the deceased was husband/wife, no ruling is given.
4
Consider the ajal (one-year respite)
If a khuntha who subsequently shows male signs does not consummate the marriage, the wife gets a one-year respite, like any other husband who does not consummate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الخنثى
لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع وله أقل النصيبين فلو مات أبوه وترك ابناً له بلوغه أو زوجة فالنكاح موقوف لا يفسد ولا يبطل ولا يتوارثان حتى يستبين أمر الخنثى لأن التوارث حكم النكاح النافذ لا حكم النكاح الموقوف، فإن زوجه الأب امرأة وبلغ وظهر علامات الرجال ونحوه حكم بجواز النكاح إلا أنه أذا لم يصل إليها فإنه يؤجل سنة كما يؤجل غيره إذا لم يصل إلى امرأته ولو أن هذا الخنثى المشكل تزوج خنثى مثله فالنكاح يكون موقوفاً إلى أن يستبين حالهما، فإن تبين حالهما فالنكاح جائز ، وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا قبل أن يزول الإشكال لم يتوارثا وإن ماتا وتركا أحد الأبوين فأقام كل واحد من ورثتهما البينة الزوج وأن الأخر هو الزوجة لا يقضى بشيء من ذلك، ولو أن رجلاً قبل هذا الخنثى بشهوة ليس لهذا الرجل أن يتزوج بمحارمه حتى بتبين أمره.

هو
قال
رحمه
الله : (فإن لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع لأن بيت المال أعد لنوائب المسلمين فيدخل في ملكه تعذراً للحاجة وهي حاجة الختان فإذا ختنته تباع ويرد ثمنها إلى بيت المال، فإذا زوج امرأة فختنته ثم طلقها جاز لأنه إن كان ذكراً صح النكاح، وإن كان أنثى فنظر الجنس أخف ثم يفرق بينهما لاحتمال أنه ذكر فيصح النكاح بينهما فتحصل الفرقة ثم تعتد إن خلا بها احتياطاً. ولو حلف بعتق أو طلاق بأن قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت طالق أو فعبدي حر فولدت خنثى لم يقع شيء حتى يستبين لأن الخنثى لم يثبت بالشك، ولو قال كل عبد لي حر أو قال كل أمة لي حرة وله مملوك خنثى لا يعتق حتى يستبين أمرء لما قلنا. وإن قال القولين جميعاً عتق للتيقن بأحد الوصفين لأنه لا يخلو عن أحدهما، وإن قال الخنثى أنا رجل وامرأة لم يقبل قوله إذا كان مشكلاً لأنه دعوى بلا دليل. وذكر في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة : إن قال الخنثى المشكل أنا ذكر أو أنثى كان القول قوله لأن الإنسان أمين في حق نفسه والقول قول الأمين ما لم يعرف خلاف ما قال ما إذا قالت المعتدة انقضت عدتي وأنكر الزوج كان القول قولها ما لم يعرف خلاف قولها بأن قلت في مدة لا تنقضي في مثلها العدة، والأولى ما ذكره في النهاية. ولا يحضر الخنثى غسل رجل ولا امرأة لاحتمال أنه ذكر قبره لأنه أن كان أنثى أقيم واجب، وإن كان ذكر لا يضره التسجية. وإذا أراد أن يصلى عليه وعلى رجل وامرأة وضع الرجل مما يلي الأمام والخنثى خلفه والمرأة خلف الخنثى، ويؤخر عن الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويقدم على المرأة لاحتمال أنه رجل. ولو دفن مع رجل في قبر واحد للعذر جعل خلف الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويجعل بينهما حاجزاً من صعيد ليكون في حكم القبرين وكذا الرجلان إذا دفنا في قبر واحد. وإن دفن مع امرأة قدم الخنثى لاحتمال أنه أنثى، ويدخل قبره ذو رحم محرم منه لاحتمال أنه أنثى. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لما يتعلق بالخنثى من الحدود والقصاص، ولا لما يتعلق به من الأيمان، ولا لما يتعلق به من الدعوى والبينة، ولا لبيان الاختلاف الواقع فيه، ولا لبيان شهادته. قال في الأصل ولو أن رجلاً قذف الخنثى المشكل قبل البلوغ أو قذف الخنثى صبي رجلاً فلأحد على القاذف، أما إذا كان القاذف هو الخنثى فلأنه أو صبية، فإما إذا كان القاذف رجلاً فلأنه غير محصن لأن البلوغ من أحد شرائط إحصان القذف كالإسلام، وإن قذف الخنثى بعد بلوغه بالسن، فإن ظهر له علامة يستدل بها على كونه ذكراً أو أنثى حد حد الرجال أو النساء، ولو قذف الخنثى رجلاً بعد ظهور علامة الرجال أو قذفه رجل فهما سواء فيجب الحد، وإن لم يظهر له علامة فلا حد على قاذفه. وهذا لأن الخنثى وإن صار محصناً بالبلوغ إلا أنه لم يظهر عليه علامة الأنوثة أو الذكورة يجوز أن يكون هذا رجلاً وأن يكون امرأة، فإن كان امرأة فهو بمنزلة الرتقاء لأنها لا تجامع كالرتقاء. ومن قذف رجلاً محبوباً أو امرأة رتقاء لا حد عليه وإن كان الخنثى هو القاذف يحد لأنه مجبوب بالغ أو رتقاء بالغة، والمجبوب البالغ والرتقاء البالغة إذا قذف إنساناً يجب عليه الحد وإن سرق بعد ما أدرك يجب عليه الحد. وإن سرق منه ما يساوي عشرة يقطع السارق رجل أو امرأة. ولو قطع يد هذا الخنثى قبل أن يبلغ أو يستبين أمره فلا قصاص على قاطعه سواء كان القاطع رجلاً أو امرأة . وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا قتل الخنثى رجلاً أو امرأة عمداً كان عليه القصاص، وإن قطع هذا الخنثى يد رجل أو امرأة فعلى عاقلته أرش ذلك وبعد البلوغ إذا قطع يد إنسان قبل أن يستبين أمره عمداً فإنه يجب عليه الأرش. في ماله وإن شهد مغنماً يرضخ له ولا يسهم، وإن ارتد عن الإسلام قبل أن يدرك أو بعدما أدرك لا يقتل عندهم جميعاً، أما قبل فإنه صبي أو صبية وردة الصبي والصبية لا تصح عند أبي يوسف. وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد أنه وإن كان الصبي العاقل والصبية العاقلة إلا أنه لا يقتل على الردة عندهما، وبعد البلوغ تصح ردته بالإجماع إلا أنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون رجلاً أو امرأة، فإن كان رجلاً حل قتله ولا يحل إن كان امرأة فلا يحل بالشك. وإن كان من أهل الذمة لا يوضع عليه خراج رأسه حتى ويستبين أمره ولا يدخل في القسامة، ولو كان الخنثى أبوه حياً فقال هو غلام ولا يعرف ذلك إلا بقوله لكان القول قوله وكذلك لو قال هي جارية فالقول قوله إذا لم يكن مشكل الحال لأن الوصي قائم مقام الأب وإن كان مشكل الحال لم يصدق. وإن قتل الخنثى خطأ قبل أن يستبين أمره قال القول في ذلك قول القاتل أنه ذكر أو أنثى إن كانت الدية تجب على القاتل إن لم يكن له عاقلة، وإن كان له عاقلة فالقول قول العاقلة وإن قالوا لا ندري فالقول قولهم ووجب عليهم دية وإن قالوا إنه أنثى وورثة الخنثى ادعوا أنه ذكر فالقول قول العاقلة لأنهم يدعون على القاتل والعاقلة زيادة خمسة آلاف درهم والقاتل والعاقلة ينكرون ذلك فيقضى عليهم بدية المرأة ويتوقف العقل إلى أن يستبين أمره أنه ذكر أو أنثى . رجل مات وترك ذكراً وخنثى وزوجة فمات الخنثى بعد موت أبيه فادعت أم الخنثى أنه ذكر وأنه كان ورث من أبيه نصف المال بعد الثمن لأنه مات وترك ابنين وامرأة ثم مات الخنثى فورثت ثلث
Book of the Intersex. If he has no wealth, then from the treasury, then it is sold, and he gets the lesser of the two shares. If his father dies and leaves a son who reaches puberty or a wife, then the marriage is suspended—it does not become invalid nor void, and they do not inherit from each other until the matter of the intersex becomes clear, because inheritance is a ruling of effective marriage, not of suspended marriage. If the father married him to a woman and he reached puberty and signs of masculinity appeared, it is judged that the marriage is valid; except that if he did not have intercourse with her, he is given a year's respite, just as others are given a year if they do not have intercourse with their wives. If this ambiguous intersex married another like him, the marriage is suspended until their situation becomes clear. If their situation becomes clear, the marriage is valid. If one of them dies or both die before the ambiguity is resolved, they do not inherit from each other. If they both die and leave one of the parents, and each of their heirs establishes proof that the deceased was the husband and the other was the wife, nothing is ruled accordingly. If a man kisses this intersex with desire, that man may not marry the intersex's maharim until his matter becomes clear. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'If he has no wealth, then from the treasury, then it is sold, because the treasury is established for the needs of Muslims, so it enters into his ownership out of necessity for the need of circumcision. When he is circumcised, the [item] is sold and its price is returned to the treasury. If he marries a woman and then divorces her, it is valid, because if he is male, the marriage is valid; if she is female, then looking at gender is lighter; then they are separated due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage between them would be valid, resulting in separation; then she observes 'iddah if he had privacy with her, as a precaution. If he swears an oath of emancipation or divorce, saying: 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are divorced' or 'my slave is free', and she gives birth to an intersex, nothing occurs until it becomes clear, because intersex is not established by doubt. If he says 'Every male slave I own is free' or 'Every female slave I own is free' and he has an intersex slave, it is not freed until his matter becomes clear, for what we said. If he says both statements together, it is freed due to certainty of one of the two descriptions, because he is not devoid of either. If the intersex says 'I am a man and a woman', his statement is not accepted when he is ambiguous, because it is a claim without evidence. It is mentioned in al-Nihayah, citing al-Dhakhirah: If the ambiguous intersex says 'I am male' or 'I am female', his statement is accepted, because a person is trustworthy regarding himself, and the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, like when a divorced woman claims her 'iddah has ended and the husband denies, her statement is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, such as if she claims it in a period in which 'iddah cannot end. The preferable view is what al-Nihayah mentioned. The intersex does not attend the washing of a man or a woman, due to the possibility that they may be of the opposite gender. It is recommended to cover his grave with a shroud, because if she was female, it is obligatory; if male, covering does not harm him. When one intends to pray over him, and over a man and a woman, the man is placed closest to the imam, the intersex behind him, and the woman behind the intersex. He is delayed relative to the man because of the possibility he is a woman, and given precedence over the woman because of the possibility he is a man. If he is buried with a man in one grave due to necessity, he is placed behind the man because of the possibility he is a woman, and a barrier of soil is placed between them to be like two graves. Similarly for two men buried in one grave. If he is buried with a woman, the intersex is placed ahead because of the possibility she is female. Only a mahram relative enters his grave because of the possibility she is female. The author did not address rulings related to the intersex concerning hadd penalties, qisas, oaths, claims, evidence, nor the differences that occur therein, nor his testimony. He said in al-Asl: If a man accuses an ambiguous intersex of fornication before puberty, or a prepubescent boy accuses the intersex, then there is [something] regarding the accuser. If the accuser is the intersex, because he is [like] a boy or girl? If the accuser is a man, because the intersex is not muhsan, since puberty is a condition for ihsan of slander like Islam. If he accuses the intersex after puberty by age, and a sign appears indicating he is male or female, he is given the hadd of men or women. If he accuses a man after the appearance of male signs, or a man accuses him, both are the same and hadd is obligatory. If no sign appears, there is no hadd on his accuser. This is because the intersex, though muhsan by puberty, has not shown signs of femininity or masculinity; it is possible he is a man or a woman. If she is a woman, she is like a woman with vaginal occlusion (ratqa'), because she does not have intercourse. Whoever accuses a man who is impotent (majbub) or a woman with vaginal occlusion (ratqa') has no hadd. If the intersex is the accuser, he is given hadd because he is an adult impotent (majbub) or an adult woman with occlusion (ratqa'). An adult impotent or an adult woman with occlusion, if they accuse someone, hadd is obligatory on them. If he steals after reaching maturity, hadd is obligatory on him. If something worth ten dirhams is stolen from him, the thief is punished by amputation, whether man or woman. If someone cuts off the hand of this intersex before he reaches puberty or his matter becomes clear, there is no qisas on the cutter, whether the cutter is a man or a woman. Similarly, if the intersex kills a man or a woman intentionally, qisas is on him. If the intersex cuts off the hand of a man or a woman, the 'aqilah pays the compensation. After puberty, if he cuts off someone's hand intentionally before his matter becomes clear, the compensation is due from his wealth. If he testifies [as a witness in war], he is given a small portion (radhkh) and not a full share. If he apostatizes from Islam before reaching maturity or after reaching maturity, he is not killed according to all of them. Before maturity, he is a boy or girl, and apostasy of a boy or girl is not valid according to Abu Yusuf. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, even if the discerning boy and girl's apostasy is valid, he is not killed on apostasy according to them. After puberty, his apostasy is valid by consensus, but he is either a man or a woman; if he is a man, killing him is permissible; if she is a woman, it is not permissible, so it is not permissible due to doubt. If he is a dhimmi, no jizyah is imposed on him until his matter becomes clear, and he does not enter into qasamah. If the intersex's father is alive and says 'He is a boy' and this is not known except by his statement, then the statement is accepted. Similarly, if he says 'She is a girl', his statement is accepted when the situation is not ambiguous, because the guardian (wasi) stands in place of the father. If the situation is ambiguous, he is not believed. If the intersex is killed by mistake before his matter becomes clear, it is said that the statement regarding whether he is male or female is that of the killer, if the blood money is obligatory on the killer if he has no 'aqilah. If he has an 'aqilah, then the statement is that of the 'aqilah. If they say 'We do not know', their statement is accepted and they are obliged to pay the blood money. If they say 'She is female' but the heirs of the intersex claim he is male, the statement is that of the 'aqilah, because they are claiming against the killer and the 'aqilah an additional five thousand dirhams, and the killer and 'aqilah deny that, so they are ordered to pay the blood money of a woman, and the blood money is suspended until his matter becomes clear whether he is male or female. [Example:] A man dies leaving a son, an intersex, and a wife. Then the intersex dies after his father's death. The mother of the intersex claims he was male and that he inherited half the property after the [wife's] eighth from his father, because he died leaving two sons and a wife; then the intersex died, and she inherited one-third.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' on 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq', compiling rulings regarding the ambiguous intersex person (khuntha mushkil). The khuntha mushkil is one who has both male and female genitalia or neither, and whose gender cannot be determined. The passage covers several areas:

**Marriage and Inheritance:** The marriage of a khuntha mushkil is suspended (mawquf) until clarity. If he/she marries another khuntha, the marriage is also suspended. The rule of inheritance (tawaruth) only applies to a valid (nafidh) marriage, not a suspended one. Once signs appear (e.g., beard for males), the marriage becomes valid. If the khuntha does not consummate, the spouse gets a one-year respite (ajal) before the marriage can be annulled.

**Circumcision and Treasury:** If the khuntha has no money for circumcision (khitan), the treasury (bayt al-mal) provides, and the cost is recovered by selling the khuntha's property.

**Oaths and Emancipation:** Oaths conditional on the birth of a boy or girl (e.g., divorce or freeing a slave) do not take effect if the child is khuntha, because gender is uncertain. However, if someone says 'every slave I own is free' and has a khuntha slave, the slave is not freed until the khuntha's gender is clear. If both 'male' and 'female' statements are made together, the slave is freed because one must be true.

**Self-Identification:** The khuntha's own claim to be male or female is generally accepted (qawluhu qawl), as a person is trustworthy about themselves, unless contradicted by known facts (like claiming iddah ended in an impossibly short time).

**Burial and Prayer:** The khuntha is positioned between men and women in funeral prayers: behind the man but ahead of the woman. In burial, if with a man, the khuntha is placed behind with a dirt barrier; if with a woman, the khuntha is placed ahead (closer to the qibla?) due to possibility of being female. Only mahram relatives may enter the khuntha's grave.

**Hadd and Qisas:** For slander (qadhf), the khuntha is considered muhsan only after puberty and if signs of gender appear. If no signs appear, the accuser of a khuntha is not subject to hadd, because the khuntha might be like a woman with vaginal occlusion (ratqa') or an impotent man (majbub), and slandering such persons carries no hadd. However, if the khuntha is the slanderer, hadd applies because he/she is an adult. For theft, amputation applies. For injury, if the victim is a prepubescent khuntha, no qisas for the attacker; if the khuntha injures another, compensation is on the 'aqilah. After maturity, compensation is from the khuntha's own wealth.

**Testimony and Apostasy:** The khuntha receives a small share (radhkh) in war booty, not a full share. For apostasy, a prepubescent khuntha is not killed; after puberty, if male, execution is permissible; if female, not. Thus, due to doubt, execution is stayed. Dhimmis who are khuntha pay no jizyah until gender is clear. For inheritance, a case example is given: a man dies leaving a son, a khuntha, and a wife; the khuntha dies later, and the mother claims the khuntha was male, affecting the distribution.

Throughout, the core principle is caution (ihtiyat): rulings are suspended or multiple possibilities are considered until the khuntha's gender is determined.

Key Terms
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): An intersex person with ambiguous gender, impossible to determine as male or female.
نكاح موقوف (nikah mawquf): A marriage contract that is valid in principle but whose effects (like inheritance) are suspended pending gender determination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A khuntha mushkil marries a non-khuntha woman. Before any gender clarity, the khuntha dies. Does the wife inherit?
A) Yes, because the marriage contract was executed.
B) No, because the marriage was suspended and inheritance requires a fully effective marriage.
C) Yes, but only if the khuntha's father consented.
D) No, because the khuntha was not legally competent.

Key Takeaway
A khuntha's marriage is valid but its inheritance effects are suspended until gender is determined.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
7 min
Oaths, Emancipation, and Self-Identification of the Khuntha
Rulings on oaths, emancipation, and self-declaration of khuntha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rulings on oaths conditioned on the child's gender when the child is born khuntha, and evaluate the khuntha's own claim of gender.

Core Idea
Oaths lapse when gender is uncertain; a khuntha's self-identification is accepted unless contradicted.

The khuntha mushkil creates uncertainty in oaths and declarations. If a husband swears that his wife's child will be a boy (conditional divorce), and she gives birth to a khuntha, the oath does not trigger because the gender is unknown. Similarly, freeing slaves of ambiguous gender is suspended. The khuntha's own claim to be male or female is generally trusted, but not if he claims both. This lesson unpacks these rules.

Guided Path
1
Understand oaths conditioned on gender
Example: husband says 'If the child is a boy, you are divorced.' Wife gives birth to a khuntha. The divorce does not occur because the condition is not fulfilled with certainty.
Hadith? Not cited here but based on principle that uncertainty prevents enforcement.
2
Analyze rulings on freeing slaves
If a master says 'Every male slave I own is free' and has a khuntha slave, the slave is not freed until gender is clear. If he says both 'male' and 'female' statements together, the slave is freed because one must be true.
3
Evaluate the khuntha's self-identification
According to al-Nihayah, the khuntha's claim to be male or female is accepted because a person is trustworthy about themselves. However, if he claims both male and female, it is rejected as a claim without evidence.
Analogous to a divorced woman claiming her iddah ended.
4
Apply the precautionary principle
In all cases, the underlying reason is that certainty is required for severe consequences (divorce, freedom, or establishing lineage).

كتاب الخنثى
لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع وله أقل النصيبين فلو مات أبوه وترك ابناً له بلوغه أو زوجة فالنكاح موقوف لا يفسد ولا يبطل ولا يتوارثان حتى يستبين أمر الخنثى لأن التوارث حكم النكاح النافذ لا حكم النكاح الموقوف، فإن زوجه الأب امرأة وبلغ وظهر علامات الرجال ونحوه حكم بجواز النكاح إلا أنه أذا لم يصل إليها فإنه يؤجل سنة كما يؤجل غيره إذا لم يصل إلى امرأته ولو أن هذا الخنثى المشكل تزوج خنثى مثله فالنكاح يكون موقوفاً إلى أن يستبين حالهما، فإن تبين حالهما فالنكاح جائز ، وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا قبل أن يزول الإشكال لم يتوارثا وإن ماتا وتركا أحد الأبوين فأقام كل واحد من ورثتهما البينة الزوج وأن الأخر هو الزوجة لا يقضى بشيء من ذلك، ولو أن رجلاً قبل هذا الخنثى بشهوة ليس لهذا الرجل أن يتزوج بمحارمه حتى بتبين أمره.

رحمه
الله : (فإن لم يكن له مال فمن بيت المال ثم تباع لأن بيت المال أعد لنوائب المسلمين فيدخل في ملكه تعذراً للحاجة وهي حاجة الختان فإذا ختنته تباع ويرد ثمنها إلى بيت المال، فإذا زوج امرأة فختنته ثم طلقها جاز لأنه إن كان ذكراً صح النكاح، وإن كان أنثى فنظر الجنس أخف ثم يفرق بينهما لاحتمال أنه ذكر فيصح النكاح بينهما فتحصل الفرقة ثم تعتد إن خلا بها احتياطاً. ولو حلف بعتق أو طلاق بأن قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلاماً فأنت طالق أو فعبدي حر فولدت خنثى لم يقع شيء حتى يستبين لأن الخنثى لم يثبت بالشك، ولو قال كل عبد لي حر أو قال كل أمة لي حرة وله مملوك خنثى لا يعتق حتى يستبين أمرء لما قلنا. وإن قال القولين جميعاً عتق للتيقن بأحد الوصفين لأنه لا يخلو عن أحدهما، وإن قال الخنثى أنا رجل وامرأة لم يقبل قوله إذا كان مشكلاً لأنه دعوى بلا دليل. وذكر في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة : إن قال الخنثى المشكل أنا ذكر أو أنثى كان القول قوله لأن الإنسان أمين في حق نفسه والقول قول الأمين ما لم يعرف خلاف ما قال ما إذا قالت المعتدة انقضت عدتي وأنكر الزوج كان القول قولها ما لم يعرف خلاف قولها بأن قلت في مدة لا تنقضي في مثلها العدة، والأولى ما ذكره في النهاية. ولا يحضر الخنثى غسل رجل ولا امرأة لاحتمال أنه ذكر قبره لأنه أن كان أنثى أقيم واجب، وإن كان ذكر لا يضره التسجية. وإذا أراد أن يصلى عليه وعلى رجل وامرأة وضع الرجل مما يلي الأمام والخنثى خلفه والمرأة خلف الخنثى، ويؤخر عن الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويقدم على المرأة لاحتمال أنه رجل. ولو دفن مع رجل في قبر واحد للعذر جعل خلف الرجل لاحتمال أنه امرأة ويجعل بينهما حاجزاً من صعيد ليكون في حكم القبرين وكذا الرجلان إذا دفنا في قبر واحد. وإن دفن مع امرأة قدم الخنثى لاحتمال أنه أنثى، ويدخل قبره ذو رحم محرم منه لاحتمال أنه أنثى. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لما يتعلق بالخنثى من الحدود والقصاص، ولا لما يتعلق به من الأيمان، ولا لما يتعلق به من الدعوى والبينة، ولا لبيان الاختلاف الواقع فيه، ولا لبيان شهادته. قال في الأصل ولو أن رجلاً قذف الخنثى المشكل قبل البلوغ أو قذف الخنثى صبي رجلاً فلأحد على القاذف، أما إذا كان القاذف هو الخنثى فلأنه أو صبية، فإما إذا كان القاذف رجلاً فلأنه غير محصن لأن البلوغ من أحد شرائط إحصان القذف كالإسلام، وإن قذف الخنثى بعد بلوغه بالسن، فإن ظهر له علامة يستدل بها على كونه ذكراً أو أنثى حد حد الرجال أو النساء، ولو قذف الخنثى رجلاً بعد ظهور علامة الرجال أو قذفه رجل فهما سواء فيجب الحد، وإن لم يظهر له علامة فلا حد على قاذفه. وهذا لأن الخنثى وإن صار محصناً بالبلوغ إلا أنه لم يظهر عليه علامة الأنوثة أو الذكورة يجوز أن يكون هذا رجلاً وأن يكون امرأة، فإن كان امرأة فهو بمنزلة الرتقاء لأنها لا تجامع كالرتقاء. ومن قذف رجلاً محبوباً أو امرأة رتقاء لا حد عليه وإن كان الخنثى هو القاذف يحد لأنه مجبوب بالغ أو رتقاء بالغة، والمجبوب البالغ والرتقاء البالغة إذا قذف إنساناً يجب عليه الحد وإن سرق بعد ما أدرك يجب عليه الحد. وإن سرق منه ما يساوي عشرة يقطع السارق رجل أو امرأة. ولو قطع يد هذا الخنثى قبل أن يبلغ أو يستبين أمره فلا قصاص على قاطعه سواء كان القاطع رجلاً أو امرأة . وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا قتل الخنثى رجلاً أو امرأة عمداً كان عليه القصاص، وإن قطع هذا الخنثى يد رجل أو امرأة فعلى عاقلته أرش ذلك وبعد البلوغ إذا قطع يد إنسان قبل أن يستبين أمره عمداً فإنه يجب عليه الأرش. في ماله وإن شهد مغنماً يرضخ له ولا يسهم، وإن ارتد عن الإسلام قبل أن يدرك أو بعدما أدرك لا يقتل عندهم جميعاً، أما قبل فإنه صبي أو صبية وردة الصبي والصبية لا تصح عند أبي يوسف. وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد أنه وإن كان الصبي العاقل والصبية العاقلة إلا أنه لا يقتل على الردة عندهما، وبعد البلوغ تصح ردته بالإجماع إلا أنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون رجلاً أو امرأة، فإن كان رجلاً حل قتله ولا يحل إن كان امرأة فلا يحل بالشك. وإن كان من أهل الذمة لا يوضع عليه خراج رأسه حتى ويستبين أمره ولا يدخل في القسامة، ولو كان الخنثى أبوه حياً فقال هو غلام ولا يعرف ذلك إلا بقوله لكان القول قوله وكذلك لو قال هي جارية فالقول قوله إذا لم يكن مشكل الحال لأن الوصي قائم مقام الأب وإن كان مشكل الحال لم يصدق. وإن قتل الخنثى خطأ قبل أن يستبين أمره قال القول في ذلك قول القاتل أنه ذكر أو أنثى إن كانت الدية تجب على القاتل إن لم يكن له عاقلة، وإن كان له عاقلة فالقول قول العاقلة وإن قالوا لا ندري فالقول قولهم ووجب عليهم دية وإن قالوا إنه أنثى وورثة الخنثى ادعوا أنه ذكر فالقول قول العاقلة لأنهم يدعون على القاتل والعاقلة زيادة خمسة آلاف درهم والقاتل والعاقلة ينكرون ذلك فيقضى عليهم بدية المرأة ويتوقف العقل إلى أن يستبين أمره أنه ذكر أو أنثى . رجل مات وترك ذكراً وخنثى وزوجة فمات الخنثى بعد موت أبيه فادعت أم الخنثى أنه ذكر وأنه كان ورث من أبيه نصف المال بعد الثمن لأنه مات وترك ابنين وامرأة ثم مات الخنثى فورثت ثلث
Book of the Intersex. If he has no wealth, then from the treasury, then it is sold, and he gets the lesser of the two shares. If his father dies and leaves a son who reaches puberty or a wife, then the marriage is suspended—it does not become invalid nor void, and they do not inherit from each other until the matter of the intersex becomes clear, because inheritance is a ruling of effective marriage, not of suspended marriage. If the father married him to a woman and he reached puberty and signs of masculinity appeared, it is judged that the marriage is valid; except that if he did not have intercourse with her, he is given a year's respite, just as others are given a year if they do not have intercourse with their wives. If this ambiguous intersex married another like him, the marriage is suspended until their situation becomes clear. If their situation becomes clear, the marriage is valid. If one of them dies or both die before the ambiguity is resolved, they do not inherit from each other. If they both die and leave one of the parents, and each of their heirs establishes proof that the deceased was the husband and the other was the wife, nothing is ruled accordingly. If a man kisses this intersex with desire, that man may not marry the intersex's maharim until his matter becomes clear. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'If he has no wealth, then from the treasury, then it is sold, because the treasury is established for the needs of Muslims, so it enters into his ownership out of necessity for the need of circumcision. When he is circumcised, the [item] is sold and its price is returned to the treasury. If he marries a woman and then divorces her, it is valid, because if he is male, the marriage is valid; if she is female, then looking at gender is lighter; then they are separated due to the possibility that he is male, so the marriage between them would be valid, resulting in separation; then she observes 'iddah if he had privacy with her, as a precaution. If he swears an oath of emancipation or divorce, saying: 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are divorced' or 'my slave is free', and she gives birth to an intersex, nothing occurs until it becomes clear, because intersex is not established by doubt. If he says 'Every male slave I own is free' or 'Every female slave I own is free' and he has an intersex slave, it is not freed until his matter becomes clear, for what we said. If he says both statements together, it is freed due to certainty of one of the two descriptions, because he is not devoid of either. If the intersex says 'I am a man and a woman', his statement is not accepted when he is ambiguous, because it is a claim without evidence. It is mentioned in al-Nihayah, citing al-Dhakhirah: If the ambiguous intersex says 'I am male' or 'I am female', his statement is accepted, because a person is trustworthy regarding himself, and the statement of a trustworthy person is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, like when a divorced woman claims her 'iddah has ended and the husband denies, her statement is accepted as long as the contrary is not known, such as if she claims it in a period in which 'iddah cannot end. The preferable view is what al-Nihayah mentioned. The intersex does not attend the washing of a man or a woman, due to the possibility that they may be of the opposite gender. It is recommended to cover his grave with a shroud, because if she was female, it is obligatory; if male, covering does not harm him. When one intends to pray over him, and over a man and a woman, the man is placed closest to the imam, the intersex behind him, and the woman behind the intersex. He is delayed relative to the man because of the possibility he is a woman, and given precedence over the woman because of the possibility he is a man. If he is buried with a man in one grave due to necessity, he is placed behind the man because of the possibility he is a woman, and a barrier of soil is placed between them to be like two graves. Similarly for two men buried in one grave. If he is buried with a woman, the intersex is placed ahead because of the possibility she is female. Only a mahram relative enters his grave because of the possibility she is female. The author did not address rulings related to the intersex concerning hadd penalties, qisas, oaths, claims, evidence, nor the differences that occur therein, nor his testimony. He said in al-Asl: If a man accuses an ambiguous intersex of fornication before puberty, or a prepubescent boy accuses the intersex, then there is [something] regarding the accuser. If the accuser is the intersex, because he is [like] a boy or girl? If the accuser is a man, because the intersex is not muhsan, since puberty is a condition for ihsan of slander like Islam. If he accuses the intersex after puberty by age, and a sign appears indicating he is male or female, he is given the hadd of men or women. If he accuses a man after the appearance of male signs, or a man accuses him, both are the same and hadd is obligatory. If no sign appears, there is no hadd on his accuser. This is because the intersex, though muhsan by puberty, has not shown signs of femininity or masculinity; it is possible he is a man or a woman. If she is a woman, she is like a woman with vaginal occlusion (ratqa'), because she does not have intercourse. Whoever accuses a man who is impotent (majbub) or a woman with vaginal occlusion (ratqa') has no hadd. If the intersex is the accuser, he is given hadd because he is an adult impotent (majbub) or an adult woman with occlusion (ratqa'). An adult impotent or an adult woman with occlusion, if they accuse someone, hadd is obligatory on them. If he steals after reaching maturity, hadd is obligatory on him. If something worth ten dirhams is stolen from him, the thief is punished by amputation, whether man or woman. If someone cuts off the hand of this intersex before he reaches puberty or his matter becomes clear, there is no qisas on the cutter, whether the cutter is a man or a woman. Similarly, if the intersex kills a man or a woman intentionally, qisas is on him. If the intersex cuts off the hand of a man or a woman, the 'aqilah pays the compensation. After puberty, if he cuts off someone's hand intentionally before his matter becomes clear, the compensation is due from his wealth. If he testifies [as a witness in war], he is given a small portion (radhkh) and not a full share. If he apostatizes from Islam before reaching maturity or after reaching maturity, he is not killed according to all of them. Before maturity, he is a boy or girl, and apostasy of a boy or girl is not valid according to Abu Yusuf. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, even if the discerning boy and girl's apostasy is valid, he is not killed on apostasy according to them. After puberty, his apostasy is valid by consensus, but he is either a man or a woman; if he is a man, killing him is permissible; if she is a woman, it is not permissible, so it is not permissible due to doubt. If he is a dhimmi, no jizyah is imposed on him until his matter becomes clear, and he does not enter into qasamah. If the intersex's father is alive and says 'He is a boy' and this is not known except by his statement, then the statement is accepted. Similarly, if he says 'She is a girl', his statement is accepted when the situation is not ambiguous, because the guardian (wasi) stands in place of the father. If the situation is ambiguous, he is not believed. If the intersex is killed by mistake before his matter becomes clear, it is said that the statement regarding whether he is male or female is that of the killer, if the blood money is obligatory on the killer if he has no 'aqilah. If he has an 'aqilah, then the statement is that of the 'aqilah. If they say 'We do not know', their statement is accepted and they are obliged to pay the blood money. If they say 'She is female' but the heirs of the intersex claim he is male, the statement is that of the 'aqilah, because they are claiming against the killer and the 'aqilah an additional five thousand dirhams, and the killer and 'aqilah deny that, so they are ordered to pay the blood money of a woman, and the blood money is suspended until his matter becomes clear whether he is male or female. [Example:] A man dies leaving a son, an intersex, and a wife. Then the intersex dies after his father's death. The mother of the intersex claims he was male and that he inherited half the property after the [wife's] eighth from his father, because he died leaving two sons and a wife; then the intersex died, and she inherited one-third.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' on 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq', compiling rulings regarding the ambiguous intersex person (khuntha mushkil). The khuntha mushkil is one who has both male and female genitalia or neither, and whose gender cannot be determined. The passage covers several areas:

**Marriage and Inheritance:** The marriage of a khuntha mushkil is suspended (mawquf) until clarity. If he/she marries another khuntha, the marriage is also suspended. The rule of inheritance (tawaruth) only applies to a valid (nafidh) marriage, not a suspended one. Once signs appear (e.g., beard for males), the marriage becomes valid. If the khuntha does not consummate, the spouse gets a one-year respite (ajal) before the marriage can be annulled.

**Circumcision and Treasury:** If the khuntha has no money for circumcision (khitan), the treasury (bayt al-mal) provides, and the cost is recovered by selling the khuntha's property.

**Oaths and Emancipation:** Oaths conditional on the birth of a boy or girl (e.g., divorce or freeing a slave) do not take effect if the child is khuntha, because gender is uncertain. However, if someone says 'every slave I own is free' and has a khuntha slave, the slave is not freed until the khuntha's gender is clear. If both 'male' and 'female' statements are made together, the slave is freed because one must be true.

**Self-Identification:** The khuntha's own claim to be male or female is generally accepted (qawluhu qawl), as a person is trustworthy about themselves, unless contradicted by known facts (like claiming iddah ended in an impossibly short time).

**Burial and Prayer:** The khuntha is positioned between men and women in funeral prayers: behind the man but ahead of the woman. In burial, if with a man, the khuntha is placed behind with a dirt barrier; if with a woman, the khuntha is placed ahead (closer to the qibla?) due to possibility of being female. Only mahram relatives may enter the khuntha's grave.

**Hadd and Qisas:** For slander (qadhf), the khuntha is considered muhsan only after puberty and if signs of gender appear. If no signs appear, the accuser of a khuntha is not subject to hadd, because the khuntha might be like a woman with vaginal occlusion (ratqa') or an impotent man (majbub), and slandering such persons carries no hadd. However, if the khuntha is the slanderer, hadd applies because he/she is an adult. For theft, amputation applies. For injury, if the victim is a prepubescent khuntha, no qisas for the attacker; if the khuntha injures another, compensation is on the 'aqilah. After maturity, compensation is from the khuntha's own wealth.

**Testimony and Apostasy:** The khuntha receives a small share (radhkh) in war booty, not a full share. For apostasy, a prepubescent khuntha is not killed; after puberty, if male, execution is permissible; if female, not. Thus, due to doubt, execution is stayed. Dhimmis who are khuntha pay no jizyah until gender is clear. For inheritance, a case example is given: a man dies leaving a son, a khuntha, and a wife; the khuntha dies later, and the mother claims the khuntha was male, affecting the distribution.

Throughout, the core principle is caution (ihtiyat): rulings are suspended or multiple possibilities are considered until the khuntha's gender is determined.

Key Terms
أمين في حق نفسه (amin fi haqq nafsih): A person is considered trustworthy regarding their own personal status matters (like gender, iddah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A khuntha mushkil says 'I am a man.' According to the preferred view in al-Nihayah, is this statement accepted?
A) No, because the khuntha is inherently untrustworthy.
B) Yes, because a person is trustworthy about themselves.
C) No, because only a doctor can determine gender.
D) Yes, only if he has male physical signs.

Key Takeaway
A khuntha's single-gender claim is accepted; oaths conditional on gender do not trigger if the child is khuntha.

Marriage Claim on a Khuntha and Conflicting Gender Evidence
Ruling on marriage claim and gender evidence for khuntha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on accepting a marriage claim with evidence and resolve conflicting gender evidence in inheritance cases.

Core Idea
Evidence supporting a valid marriage is preferred over evidence that would invalidate it.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses a complex case: a man claims marriage to a deceased khuntha (hermaphrodite). The ruling depends on two sets of evidence: proof of the marriage contract, and conflicting evidence about the khuntha’s gender. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning that favours evidence upholding the marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and claims
Determine who is the claimant (husband), who are the opponents (brother, mother), and what evidence each brings. The husband brings evidence of a marriage contract and also evidence that the khuntha was female.
The khuntha is deceased; the claim involves inheritance.
2
Analyse the first scenario: marriage evidence accepted
When the husband brings evidence that the khuntha's father married him to the khuntha for a known dower, and the mother does not counter with evidence, the husband's claim is accepted. He must pay the dower and inherits as a husband. The mother inherits from the dower and the estate.
This applies whether the brother confirms or denies the marriage.
3
Analyse the second scenario: conflicting gender evidence
If the brother brings evidence that the khuntha urinated as a male, but the husband brings evidence that she urinated as a female, the husband's evidence is preferred. The brother's evidence is rejected.
The preference is based on upholding the marriage (istishab al-nikah).
4
Understand the underlying principle
The Hanafi school gives priority to evidence that supports the validity of the marriage over evidence that would nullify it. This aligns with the legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and the presumption of continuity of the marriage contract.
This ruling prevents the invalidation of a marriage based on gender ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أقام رجل البينة أن أبا الخنثى كان زوجها منه على ألف درهم وطلب ميراثها وصدقه الابن أو كذبه ولم تقم الأم البينة أن أب الخنثى على ما ادعت فإنه يقبل قول الزوج ويجعل عليه المهر وورث من الخنثى ميراث الزوج وورث أم الخنثى من الصداق الذي يبقى على الزوج وما ترك الخنثى. وإن أقام الأخ بينة على ما ادعت أنه كان يبول من مبال الرجال ولا يبول من مبال النساء إن أقام الزوج البينة أنها كانت أنثى وتبول من مبال النساء ولا تبول من مبال الرجال كانت بينة الأخ أولى بالرد
And if a man brings evidence that the father of the khuntha married him (the khuntha) to him (the man) for one thousand dirhams, and he requests her inheritance, and the son (the khuntha's brother) believes him or denies him, and the mother does not bring evidence that the father of the khuntha was as she claimed, then the statement of the husband is accepted, and the dower is made incumbent upon him, and he inherits from the khuntha the inheritance of a husband, and the mother of the khuntha inherits from the dower that remains upon the husband and from what the khuntha left. And if the brother brings evidence supporting his claim that the khuntha used to urinate from the place of men and did not urinate from the place of women, but the husband brings evidence that she was female and urinates from the place of women and not from the place of men, then the evidence of the brother is more deserving to be rejected.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a man claims he was married to a khuntha (who has died). He brings evidence that the khuntha's father married them. The khuntha's brother may confirm or deny. If the mother (who would inherit from the khuntha) does not counter with evidence, the husband's claim is accepted. He must pay the dower (mahr) and then inherits as a husband (1/4 if no child, but here no child mentioned). The mother inherits from the dower and the estate. If there is conflicting evidence about the khuntha's gender from urination signs, the evidence of the brother (claiming male) is given priority over the husband's evidence of female? The text says 'bayanat al-akh awla bi al-radd' meaning the brother's evidence is more deserving of rejection. So the husband's evidence prevails, supporting the marriage. This is because the husband's evidence that the khuntha was female supports the validity of the marriage, while the brother's evidence of maleness would invalidate it. The ruling prefers the evidence that upholds the marriage (istishab al-nikah).

Key Terms
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite or person with ambiguous genitalia.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.
الرد (al-radd): Rejection, as in rejecting evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens when the husband brings evidence of the marriage contract and the mother does not counter?
A) The husband's claim is accepted, he pays the mahr, and inherits as a husband.
B) The brother's statement decides the case.
C) The mother inherits everything.
D) The case is dismissed due to ambiguity.

Key Takeaway
Evidence that upholds the validity of a marriage is given priority over evidence that would nullify it, even in cases of gender ambiguity.
